(2) Does the Japanese army intend to invade Rehe? (3) Zhang Xueliang has already prepared defenses in Rehe. What is the strength of the Japanese army in Jinzhou? (4) Where is the border of Manchuria? Kobayashi's answers are not detailed.

Puyi Under Japanese Surveillance 78

Painful words from an elderly former official after visiting Puyi

Puyi's tone was extremely unnatural during the meeting.

A correspondent from Hailar reports that a former elderly official was recently summoned by Puyi to Changchun to pay his respects to the so-called puppet state's head of state. Before his departure, he was overjoyed. However, upon his return yesterday, those who saw him found him constantly frowning and sighing. When asked about the reason, he sighed for a long time and spoke about the current situation of the puppet state of Changchun as follows (the following is the elderly former official's account): "I was a second-rank official in the late Qing Dynasty. After the revolution, I retired to business, valuing my reputation of indifference to fame and fortune. I settled in the Northeast, and have always been divorced from politics. During Zhang Zuolin's time, although he remembered his favor toward me, and repeatedly and firmly invited me to take on certain positions, I always refused. This time, with the creation of the Manchurian State, although I had no desire to pursue power, I was swayed by rumors. I had heard the Qing dynasty was being restored, so I repeatedly received letters from old friends in Changchun inviting me to build the country. I could not help but be moved. Recently, I received a handwritten edict from the Xuantong Emperor summoning me, so I decided to go and pay my respects, in order to view the reconstructed Manchurian homeland. After arriving in Changchun, what shocked me was that there were Japanese everywhere, and there was no government office without Japanese. Even at the gate of important government offices, there were Japanese and Koreans inside, interrogating visiting guests repeatedly, like customs officials checking for contraband. Furthermore, they showed no politeness. The guests stood while they sat, like prisoners being interrogated. The procedure to see the Xuantong Emperor was even more complicated. His residence was in the former Changchun Municipal Preparatory Office. Inside and outside the gate, besides the guards, there were plainclothes Japanese military police. Ordinary people are never allowed to see the head of state, and are instead seen by the Chief Secretary Komai. These were not orders issued by the head of state, but were completely deceived by the Japanese in order to control the emperor and command the feudal lords. Because I was summoned, I was spared Komai's substitute meeting. However, I first had to register at the Personnel Department, stating my resume and what I wanted to discuss. I filled it out clearly, and then the Personnel Department submitted it to the advisor, who signed and approved it. I was not allowed to see him that day, but was ordered to go the next morning at ten o'clock. I still went to the Personnel Department, and they led me to the head of state's office. At that time, the Xuantong Emperor was standing in the room, accompanied by two Japanese and two Japanese military officers. After I saluted, the Xuantong Emperor only said, 'It is good that you have come. The country is currently lacking people. You can go and meet Premier Zheng and Chief Secretary Komai, and submit your resume to the Personnel Department for review. If there are no problems, you can be appointed to a position.' When he spoke, his tone was extremely unnatural, and every time he said a word, he looked to the two Japanese on his left and right, as if he did not dare to fully express his thoughts. I said that I was currently engaged in business, and I was old and decaying, and I would not dare to take on heavy responsibilities again, and would not lead the country astray. Furthermore, the current agencies in various places are unable to handle affairs, and I am afraid that I would be difficult to manage. When I said this, the Xuantong Emperor's face changed suddenly, and he gestured with his eyes, not wanting me to say any more. At this point, the two Japanese companions seemed to resent me for not speaking correctly. They told Xuantong that the time was too long and asked him to dismiss me. Thus, without waiting for Xuantong to speak, they urged me to leave. When I left the room, I looked at the Emperor, my eyes filled with tears. I looked hesitant. At that moment, I felt a pang of sadness, and tears almost welled up in my eyes. I quickly bowed my head and hurried out. When I returned to the outer room and the Personnel Department, the Japanese head of the department came out to see me, and said with a stern face, 'The head of state summoned you to come because he intended to entrust you with relief work. Now, after an investigation by this department, it has been found that you embezzled funds when you were in charge of charity, so you cannot be appointed. How many days do you plan to stay here? If there is nothing to do, you can leave quickly.' I did not answer, but hurriedly left the room. That night, I packed my bags and returned in a hurry. I could not close my eyes on the car. Every time I closed my eyes, the Xuantong Emperor's sad face appeared before me. People say that the Manchurian State is a puppet government. I did not believe it at first, but after witnessing it once, I believed the rumors. I am afraid that the Xuantong Emperor is not even as good as a puppet, but just another Zhang Bangchang and Emperor Huizong and Emperor Qinzong of Song! I also heard people say that Japan will unify the four-headed political system and send Mutō as a general to supervise the Northeast. Currently, Komai is ordering the head of state to write an encouragement to urge Mutō to come quickly. The Japanese officials in Changchun, even those in the lower positions of bureau and department heads, surpass the actual heads. Matters large and small are all handled by Komai, Ōhashi Tadashi (Deputy Foreign Minister), Sakatani (Deputy Finance Minister), Nakano (Director of the Internal Affairs Department), Katakura (Staff Colonel of the Military Administration Department), and others. Premier Zheng Xiaoxu is like a gourd tied but uneaten. The rest are even worse, and no one pays them any attention. Recently, there is a so-called advanced official training school in Changchun, with the head of state as the president. Officials above the section chief level from various government agencies are required to attend. Every day, Japanese and traitors give lectures on: (1) the politics of Wangdao (the Kingly Way), lectured by Zheng Xiaoxu; (2) general national policies, lectured by Director Komai; (3) finance, lectured by Deputy Director Sakatani; (4) law, lectured by Director Abiru; (5) diplomacy, lectured by Deputy Director Ōhashi; (6) internal administration, lectured by Director Nakano; (7) national defense, lectured by Staff Officer Nikura; (8) health, lectured by Professor Miura of the Medical University; (9) the cultural history of Manchuria, lectured by Eto, the director of the Fengtian Library. Although the Japanese use people without integrity as puppets, they cannot trust them for long. If there is any hidden complaint, they will think of using decisive means of punishment. Zhao Xinbo and Yuan Jinkai are both in Changchun. One is nominally the Speaker of the Legislative Yuan, but where do the laws come from? They are all promulgated by the Japanese Kwantung Army, using his name to issue announcements. The other is a councilor, but he is not allowed to participate in any deliberations. These two have also lost their freedom. Recently, Yu Shencheng, who is in charge of military administration and suppressing bandits, and Bao Guancheng, the puppet mayor of Harbin, have been dismissed due to mutual accusations that made the Japanese suspicious. Those who become officials in the Manchurian State are gradually realizing the lesson that 'when the cunning rabbit dies, the hunting dog is cooked.' Therefore, they are all negative, thinking of ways to redeem themselves. Even Xi Qia and Yu Shencheng are the same. When these people turn against the Japanese, it depends on whether the central government gives them a chance to reform themselves. When I left Changchun, someone sent me to the station and firmly begged me to find a way to clear their name, so that they could be reborn. This shows the general mentality." (July 21st)

Li Siguang Talks About Reorganizing National Central University 79

Nanjing dispatch: Li Siguang told reporters, "My appointment to the Reorganization Committee of National Central University was forced upon me by the circumstances and was an unavoidable and temporary task. The outside world often mistakenly believes that I am the acting president, but this misunderstands the intention of the Executive Yuan's resolution. Although I have made this clear before, misunderstandings persist, so I must reiterate it. Since President Duan resigned, National Central University has been without a president, so the Reorganization Committee had to temporarily take over the president's responsibilities. However, the Reorganization Committee cannot reside in National Central University to handle school affairs, so the Executive Yuan appointed one member of the Reorganization Committee, after consulting with the committee, to act as president. This is an expedient measure and should not be prolonged. Professors are the ultimate masters of a university, and their fate should be in their own hands. Unfortunately, National Central University experienced an extraordinary accident. The masters were unable to resolve the crisis before it occurred. After it erupted, they were not allowed to participate in the aftermath, which is deeply regrettable. In the future, we should strive to remedy the situation, quickly conclude the reorganization work, and restore the school's regular organization to a healthy state, allowing it to resolve all its own problems. Everything at National Central University has come to a standstill, and there is much to be done. For a time, I felt overwhelmed. I now only hope that everyone will be patient and try to complete all pending matters within half a month. To get to the root of the problem requires the government's sincerity and the professors' determination. This time, the Reorganization Committee of National Central University has decided to allocate 50% of the funds for equipment. I strongly agree with this principle, but how to allocate the funds in detail requires further discussion. Monthly reports of actual income and expenses must be created as permanent records and discussion materials. Universities are institutions for exploring academic knowledge and should not be disturbed in the slightest, lest it disrupt thinking. In recent years, domestic and international political disputes have invisibly affected schools, or even originated in schools. Society only knows to condemn its evils, but does not understand its underlying causes. When politics is not on track, schools become unstable. When schools are in turmoil, it directly or indirectly makes it more difficult for politics to get on track. In my opinion, schools are not suitable places for actual political movements. Forcing it will ultimately lead to self-destruction. As for academic factionalism, it is entirely based on different academic viewpoints. If it is combined with superficial interests and affiliations, then it is not worth mentioning. I am not very familiar with the situation at National Central University, but I believe that the difficulties at National Central University may not lie here. If we consider all universities in the country, some are indeed suffering from this problem. The only solution is for everyone to devote all their efforts to academic pursuits. Then these disputes will resolve themselves. National Central University already has several kinds of research publications, which show this spirit. In the future, we should expand this to fill the entire school with academic air, so that those who occupy the name of the highest institution of learning in the central government, will truly be the highest institution of learning." (July 28th)

Wind and Rain Cause Disaster in Boshan County, Shandong Province 80

The light railway is mostly destroyed.

Many people drowned.

Jinan dispatch: Since the beginning of summer, there has been continuous rain in this province. The rain on the 25th was the heaviest. According to a telegram from Boshan County, there was a wild wind and heavy rain that night, and mountain floods broke out. The area near the train station became a swamp. The 12-li light railway from Boshan Station to the coal mine was mostly destroyed by the floodwaters. Many steel rails were also washed away. Countless houses collapsed, and electric poles fell to the ground. Because it was at night, residents who did not have time to escape were drowned. The river in Yuhang Street and the hygienic pool bathing pool outside the West Weimen gate, which is usually less than half a foot deep, is now a vast expanse of water. There are many floating corpses in the river. By the morning of the 26th, the water gradually receded, but the light railway was cut off, and coal transportation was completely blocked. Repairs will take time, and the losses are still being investigated. Last night, a large number of refugees from Boshan came to Jinan on the third Jiaoji train. They said that their fields and houses had all been washed away. The Liushan Street area, which is a recreation ground, was the site of a performance by the Qunying Society from Beiping. That night, just as the music was in full swing, the mountain flood suddenly came. The audience did not have time to escape and were mostly washed away by the water. The cries and wails shook the area for several li. It was unbearable to hear. The Jiaoji Railway's electric light room was fortunate to have a tall surrounding wall, otherwise it would also have been washed away. It is said that the mountain flood was caused by heavy rain in the Laiwu area, and the mountain flood flowed north along the river, causing this tragedy. (July 27th)

Minutes of the All-China Postal Union Conference 81

Resolutions of the Third Day

The All-China Postal Workers' Union Joint Conference held its third general meeting at 9:00 a.m. on the 27th, with more than 50 representatives in attendance, chaired by Wang Xingcang. Matters discussed: (1) The postal workers' union should send representatives to participate in the management committee of the postal pension and relief fund. Resolution: Approved in principle, and the General Assembly's Preparatory Committee will handle the matter of sending representatives. (2) Post offices nationwide should build their own buildings. Resolution: Approved in principle, and the postal authorities are recommended to review and approve it. (3) All equipment used by post offices and postal workers nationwide should be made in China as much as possible. Resolution: 1. Approved in principle, and the General Assembly will send a letter to the General Bureau and the Supply Department to pay attention to the implementation. 2. Telegraph all local unions to adopt it as much as possible. (4) Petition the government to ban private postal agencies to unify authority and promote development. Resolution: Approved in principle, and petition the National Government to strictly ban them. (5) The daily working hours for postal workers nationwide should be uniformly limited to no more than eight hours. Resolution: Approved in principle. 1. The General Assembly will send a letter to the Postal General Bureau to review and implement it. 2. There should be a clear provision in the Postal Guidelines. (6) Vacancies of postal workers in various places nationwide should be filled immediately to facilitate work. Resolution: The General Assembly will send a letter to the Postal General Bureau to review and implement it according to the following principles: 1. Vacancies of certain grades of employees should be filled by employees of the same grade (replacing members with members, and assistants with assistants). 2. Replacements should not be promoted to fill vacancies for a long time. (7) There are many points in the Postal Guidelines that are obstructive and should be revised. Resolution: 1. Petition the Ministry of Communications to revise them separately. 2. The General Assembly will designate the Beijing and Shanghai unions to send representatives to participate in the revision. (8) Expand postal services by adding bureaus and offices to actively develop postal services. Resolution: Recommend that the Ministry of Communications adopt and implement it. (9) Stamps, postal money orders, paper money, and all other printed items should be printed in China. Resolution: Recommend that the Ministry of Communications implement it as soon as possible. (10) Postal finances should be absolutely transparent. Resolution: 1. Send a letter to the Postal General Bureau to publish the budget and final accounts. 2. Postal workers have the right to inquire about accounts. (11) The current organizational law of the Postal General Bureau has many points that are obstructive and difficult to implement, and it should be politically modified to benefit postal services. Resolution: Approved in principle. 1. Restore the original three departments of performance evaluation, auditing, and secretariat, making a total of eight departments. The directors of each department should be appointed from within the bureau. 2. Abolish the Chief Secretary, and the affairs should still be handled by the Secretariat. 3. The number of department members should be appointed based on the needs of the office, and the number should not be limited. 4. Hold bureau meetings, and the postal workers' union should be allowed to send representatives to participate. (12) Union workers should be granted special leave for union affairs. Resolution: Approved in principle, and petition the central government to instruct the National Government to instruct the Ministry of Communications to review and implement it. (13) Organize a national consumer cooperative for postal workers. Resolution: Approved in principle. The meeting adjourned at 12:00 noon. The meeting continued in the afternoon, and the proposals are still being compiled. Furthermore, the first and second meetings of the association resolved to issue a declaration to safeguard postal rights in the Northeast, and telegraphed condolences to postal workers in the Northeast, and telegraphed the Postal Economic System Research Committee. The various telegrams have been drafted by the Secretariat of the General Assembly and were sent separately on the 27th.

Jiangsu Provincial Government Revises Business Tax Rates 82

Temporarily Divided into Three Types

The Jiangsu Provincial business tax rate, having undergone revision at the 514th meeting of the Provincial Government, is temporarily divided into three types: 0.5%, 0.8%, and 1%. For businesses with capital around 500 yuan, or a business turnover of 1,000 yuan or more, the minimum annual tax is 5 yuan. The details are listed below:

Type 1: Based on Total Business Income

Category A: (1) Merchandise Sales Industry, further divided into: Grain Businesses, Firewood/Charcoal/Coal Businesses, Oil & Salt Shops, Cotton Businesses, Cotton Fabric Businesses, Hemp Fabric Businesses, Oil Businesses, Bamboo & Timber Businesses, Paper Businesses, Mountain Produce & Local Specialty Businesses, Sauce Garden Businesses, Ironware Businesses, Medicinal Herb Businesses, Bamboo/Timber/Palm/Rattan Ware Businesses, Brick/Tile/Lime/Stone Businesses, Packaging Paper Box Businesses, Umbrella/Mat Businesses, Ceramic Ware Businesses, Clothing Chest Businesses, Shoe/Hat/Sock Businesses, Secondhand Clothing Businesses, Pastry Businesses, Straw Weaving Businesses, Silk Fabric Businesses, Silkworm Cocoon Businesses, Fruit Businesses, Comb Businesses, Yarn Businesses, Tea/Lacquer Businesses, North-South Goods Businesses, Copper/Tin Ware Businesses, Fan Businesses, Cured Meat/Fish Businesses, Egg Businesses, Tanned Hide/Fur/Bone Businesses, Candle/Soap Businesses, Match Businesses. (2) Transportation Industry. (3) Transport Industry. (4) Contracting Industry. (5) Electricity Industry. (6) Restaurant, Teahouse, Inn, Bathhouse, Barber Shop Industries. The applicable tax rate is 1%, temporarily reduced to 0.5%.

Category B: (1) Merchandise Sales Industry, further divided into: Imported & General Merchandise, Paint, Cement, Sugar, Hardware, Western Medicine, Lace, Electrical Materials, Candy/Tea/Food/Canned Goods, Soda/Ice Food, Felt/Carpet, etc. businesses. (2) Rental Goods Businesses. The applicable tax rate is 1%, temporarily reduced to 0.8%.

Category C: (1) Merchandise Sales Industry, further divided into: Leather, Rubber, Ham, Woolen Cloth, Western Suits, Embroidery, Ginseng/Bird's Nest, Clock/Eyeglasses, Leather Goods, Jewelry, Cosmetics/Artwork, Antiques, Incense/Candles/Paper Firecrackers, Western-style Furniture, Rosewood Furniture, Dental Fillings, Gramophones, Paper Funeral Items, Fertilizer, etc. Businesses. (2) Photography Industry. (3) Brokerage Industry of Exchanges. (4) Securities Industry. (5) Entertainment Venue Industry. The applicable tax rate is 1%, temporarily reduced to 1%.

(Note): For businesses not listed above, Article 11 of the Jiangsu Provincial Temporary Business Tax Regulations should be followed.

Type 2: Based on Business Turnover and Capital

Category A: (1) Manufacturing Industry, further divided into: Oil Presses, Silk Weaving, Cotton Weaving, Hemp Weaving, Straw Weaving, Paper Making, Brick/Tile/Lime/Stone, Silkworm Seed, Wood Plank Manufacturing, Copper/Tin/Ironware, Stationery, Cotton Ginning, Oil Pressing, Candle/Soap, Ceramic Ware, Dyeing & Weaving, Dye Houses, Repair of Goods/Equipment, Flour Mills, Smelting, Steel Machinery, Silk Reeling Factories, Button/Toothbrush Factories, etc. (2) Printing/Publishing and Books/Stationery/Educational Supplies Industry. The applicable tax rate is 1%, temporarily reduced to 0.5%.

Category B: (1) Manufacturing Industry, further divided into: Sugar Making, Vinegar Making, Lace, Aquatic Products, Wool Weaving, Shipbuilding, Vehicle Manufacturing, Sand Casting, Tea Making, Parasol Factories, Egg Yolk/Egg White, Lacquer Ware, Interior Decoration, etc. (2) Warehouse Industry. The applicable tax rate is 1%, temporarily reduced to 0.8%.

Category C: (1) Manufacturing Industry, further divided into: Candy/Food/Canned Goods, Pharmaceutical Manufacturing, Leather Manufacturing, Rubber Manufacturing, Ice Making, Gold/Silverware, Western-style & Rosewood Furniture, Soda, Toys, Cosmetics & Artwork, Ivory Utensils, etc. (2) Money Exchange Industry. (3) Insurance Industry. The applicable tax rate is 1%, temporarily reduced to 1%.

(Note): For businesses not listed above, Article 11 of the Jiangsu Provincial Temporary Business Tax Regulations should be followed.

Local Correspondence

Songjiang 83

Request to Open Alleys to Facilitate Firefighting: Since the Da Feng store carelessly caused a fire at the beginning of the month, which spread to neighboring businesses, including Tang Sanju Shoe Store, Tang Zhimin, the owner of Tang Sanju store, recognizing that West Outer Street is a prosperous commercial area with narrow alleys, making it difficult for two people to pass while carrying water for firefighting, deemed it a shortcoming. At the second meeting of the County Chamber of Commerce, Tang Zhimin, as a member, submitted a written proposal, suggesting that in order to improve firefighting efficiency, the owner of Da Feng store should open a public alley during the reconstruction of the original building to facilitate firefighting. He also submitted a request to the County Government for approval. County Magistrate Shen has now submitted the case to the County Administration Meeting for discussion and resolution, instructing the County Chamber of Commerce to inform the owner of Da Feng store to comply. It remains to be seen whether the property owner will comply with the order to open an alley.

Kunshan 84

County Government Executes Bandits: Regarding the case of Gu Pinliang's family in Dujiagang, Zhengyi, a town under the jurisdiction of the county, being robbed and murdered by bandits the other day, the county government dispatched detectives and apprehended the main culprit, Xu Bainian, a local, and five accomplices, including Zhu Qiaosheng. After repeated interrogations, Xu confessed to conspiring to rob the Gu family. The county sentenced Xu to death and submitted the case to the Provincial Government for review. On the 27th, County Magistrate Cheng received the Provincial Government's telegram of approval. At 11:00 AM, he ascended the criminal court, ordered the police to bring the prisoner for verification, bind him according to the law, and escort him to the foothills of Ma'anshan for execution by firing squad.

Taicang 85

Agricultural School Student Drowns While Bathing: Lu Yilian, a second-year student at Taicang County Rural Normal School, went to bathe in the nearby river alone after submitting his exam papers the other day. Due to a moment of carelessness, he slipped and fell into the water. By the time people noticed and tried to find him, he had already drowned. The school authorities notified the student's family to prepare a coffin for burial.

Changzhou-Wuxi Gangs of Wheat Boats Brawls: The main agricultural product of this county in spring is wheat, and the annual export volume is very large. It is transported and sold to other ports by boatmen from Changzhou and Wuxi gangs. The other day, more than ten wheat boats from Changzhou and Wuxi gangs arrived at Zhintang Town under the county's jurisdiction to load goods and dock at the east and west ends of the town. For some unknown reason, the crew members of both sides had a quarrel, which escalated into a brawl with weapons. Many were injured in the melee. The villagers rushed to report to the Water Police Squad. Captain Yin Gengcai immediately led a team of police officers to suppress the violence, disarmed both sides, and arrested two ringleaders to be taken to the squad for interrogation.

Wuxi 86

Measures to Relieve Farmers: Wuxi has always been famous for its silk production, but in recent years, there have been consecutive crop failures. This year, it is even worse after last year's flood, causing the rural economy to collapse completely, with a significant impact on society. He Yushu, Director of the Jiangsu Department of Industry, recognizing this, has repeatedly come to Wuxi to invite local figures, together with County Magistrate Chen, to discuss countermeasures and jointly seek relief measures. He has also dispatched Inspector Hua Yinchun to be stationed in Wuxi permanently to liaise with all parties and discuss plans. Ding Songlin, Director of the Agricultural Improvement Station, has also drafted a complete plan to revitalize the rural economy using agricultural funds, starting with the current autumn silkworm season. Forty silkworm rearing guidance centers will be set up throughout the county. After careful consultation with Gu Shuzhi, Director of the Farmers Bank, it has been decided to proceed with the plan. Assistance has also been obtained from major silk factories such as Dingchang, Huaxin, and Ganshen, which will set up branches in various villages, and the progress is very smooth. Regarding the improvement of various agricultural aspects, Director He Yushu has also agreed that the funds will be set at 5,000 yuan. It is planned to use 2,514 yuan from the agricultural funds and 2,486 yuan from the remaining funds of 6,142 yuan for various agricultural expenses in Xiyi in the 20th year, making a total of 5,000 yuan. The plan has been submitted to the county government and forwarded to the department for record. In order to carry out the plan precisely, a silkworm rearing guidance discussion meeting was held yesterday at the County Girls' Middle School in Xiaolou Lane. Representatives from the Department of Industry Zhou Juesheng, silkworm experts Zou Jingheng and Zheng Haiquan, and Gu Shuzhi from the Farmers Bank jointly conducted detailed discussions.

Rogue Murders Someone: Liu Zhenhan, a local rogue from Panzhuang Village, Chongren Township, the 17th District (Fuan Township) of Wuxi, recently had a feud with Bao Sheng, the son of widow Liu Gong of the same village. On May 30th, he lured Bao Sheng to his home to stay overnight. He also sent three others, posing as members of the Zhouqiao Security Corps, armed with weapons, to surround Liu Zhenhan's house at night. They pretended that Bao Sheng was suspected of theft, arrested him, ordered a farm worker to tie his hands behind his back, dragged him to a deserted field outside the door, strangled him to death with a rope, and then hired a boat from a Zhu to transport the body to Dongshanzhu at the mouth of Taihu Lake and bury it, hoping to cover up the crime. However, since her son went missing, Liu Gong has been searching everywhere without any trace. Only recently did Liu Bingcheng, a citizen of the township, find out the truth. He came to the city with Gong the other day and secretly reported to the Public Security Bureau, requesting an arrest. Director Hua immediately dispatched Detective Dai Shouquan, leading the entire team of detectives, to the countryside overnight. They successively arrested the murderers Liu Zhenhan, Xie Yucen, Xie Qiaogen, and Xie Weiqing. Several others had already fled upon hearing the news. Detective Dai escorted the four criminals to the city and handed them over to the Public Security Bureau to await transfer to the court for investigation.

Nantong 87

First Batch of Pardoned Prisoners Released: Nantong No. 4 Prison, acting on orders to handle the amnesty, is releasing the first batch of Wang Fushan, Zhu Guangmao, Zhu Chuan, Qian Xiaopu, Peng Ruiqing, Guan Yongcheng, Zhang Zhi, etc., who meet the amnesty regulations, after review by the Nantong County Court. It is estimated that there are more than 300 people who meet the requirements for commutation, and they are currently being reviewed.

Bandit Killed En Route in Jinsha: Xu Yunbiao, a bandit from Jinsha, was captured by the authorities after being hunted down. He was escorted to the city on the 26th, but escaped en route. The escorting police killed him.

Yangzhou 88

Murder Due to Extortion: A villager named Hua Guobao from Zhaoguan Dam, Shaobo, in the county was beaten to death the other day due to extortion. The deceased's brother, Chuanbao, came to the city yesterday to request an examination by the prosecutor's office of the court. Today (the 28th), Prosecutor Li Fen, along with forensic officials and police officers, went to conduct the examination to gather evidence for the arrest and interrogation of the murderer.

Wheat Boat Robbed on Luyang Lake: Wang Zhishun, a resident of Qishu Temple, makes a living by selling wheat. He often goes to various merchants in Lujin to peddle his goods, transporting them by boat two or three times a day. The other day (the 25th), at 3:00 PM, after selling all his goods, he was returning home when he passed through the heart of Luyang Lake. Suddenly, a bandit boat approached. Four bandits, each armed with a pistol, boarded the boat and looted it, taking away 150 yuan in wheat money. They then fired a shot in the air to show their force and fled eastward.

Xiashi 89

Measures to Punish Profiteers: The case of Cai Zhengxiang, a profiteer in Xiashi, privately selling Japanese yarn and inciting a crowd to rob goods has been reported in various newspapers in Shanghai and Hangzhou. It is now learned that the Provincial Party Headquarters, after receiving the report, considered the circumstances serious and specially dispatched Guan Xiaoxian to Xiashi to jointly investigate the truth with Zhan Yongquan and Yu Yunzhai, members of the Haiyan County Party Headquarters. After completing the investigation, they participated in the 20th standing committee meeting of the Xiashi Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association. It was decided that the evidence of Cai Zhengxiang's private sale of Japanese yarn was confirmed and that, in accordance with Article 2 of the Zhejiang Province Temporary Rules for Punishing Profiteers Who Privately Transport and Sell Japanese Goods, the original goods should be confiscated and a fine of more than twice the value of the goods (totaling 2,000 yuan) should be imposed. For obstructing the inspection and gathering a crowd to disrupt the anti-Japanese national salvation work, it should be handled in accordance with Article 3. Both of the above items are limited to being presented to the meeting before July 28th to await punishment. If he fails to arrive within the time limit, a reward will be posted in the newspaper for his arrest and execution. After the resolution was made, Cai Zhengxiang was immediately notified, and a letter was sent to the Xiashi Public Security Bureau requesting assistance. Meanwhile, personnel were assigned to compile a special publication to fully disclose all aspects of the case, so that the public could understand the truth of the case and be warned.

Hangzhou 90

Telegraph Operator on the Pinghan Railway Commits Suicide: On the 23rd, a traveler named He Qing from Zhejiang Province, about 20 years old, a telegraph operator on the Pinghan Railway, arrived at the West Lake First Hotel on Huashi Road, New Market in Hangzhou. After staying for two nights, he moved to the Huanhu Hotel. He went in and out as usual, and on the night of the 25th, he bought lychees. He went to sleep two hours after eating them. The room attendant suddenly heard a groan, pushed the door open, and saw the guest's face turn pale. He immediately reported to the accounting room. The guest was unable to speak and was sent to Guangji Hospital. The hospital refused to accept him. He was sent to Hangzhou Hospital for treatment, but it was ineffective, and he died soon after. The Hangzhou District Court, after being reported, dispatched a prosecutor to lead police officers to investigate and confirmed that he had died by taking poison. However, what kind of poison he took could not be determined immediately. Upon inspecting his suitcase, there were only a few pieces of clothing, four small silver coins, and more than ten copper coins. There was no suicide note. A coffin has been prepared for burial.

Local News

Minister Song Arrives in Shanghai Again Yesterday 91

Regarding the Northeast Customs and Abolition of Tael and Adoption of Dollar Issues: According to the Central News Agency, Minister of Finance Song Ziwen was originally scheduled to fly from Nanjing to Wuhan yesterday morning to report to Chairman Chiang Kai-shek on the progress of negotiations in Shanghai regarding the abolition of the tael and adoption of the dollar and other financial issues. However, due to the Northeast Customs blockade issue, which has been approved by the Central Political Conference and urgently needs to be implemented, Song flew from Nanjing to Shanghai at 6:00 AM yesterday morning on the Sikorsky aircraft, arriving in Shanghai at approximately 8:00 AM. He went directly to his private residence on Qiqi Road. Feeling slightly unwell, he immediately called upon British doctor McKinley for treatment.

Accompanying Personnel: The Sikorsky aircraft that Song used to come to Shanghai was piloted by two American aviation instructors. Those who came with Song included Yang Ge, Western advisor to the Ministry of Finance, Secretary Huang Chundao, and five others. Song took off from Nanjing at 6:00 AM yesterday morning and arrived at Longhua Airport at approximately 8:00 AM. Song's guards were waiting at the airport. Since Song's visit to Shanghai was not notified in advance, very few people outside knew about it.

Song Feels Slightly Unwell: Song felt slightly unwell due to catching a cold during the flight. At 3:30 PM, he invited British doctor McKinley from No. 41 Albert Road for treatment. According to Dr. McKinley, after examining Song's illness, he told the Central News Agency reporter that Song's illness was due to catching a cold during the journey and was not serious. He would recover within a day or two.

Refuses to See Guests: After returning to his residence, Song, feeling unwell, immediately informed his family to refuse to see guests. Therefore, Zhu Tingqi, Director of the Salt Affairs Administration, and others visited one after another but were not received. However, Tang Hai'an, Superintendent of the Jianghai Customs, was summoned by Song at 1:00 PM yesterday afternoon and did not leave until 5:30 PM.

Mission in Shanghai: According to the Central News Agency reporter's investigation of Song's mission in Shanghai: (1) The Northeast Customs blockade issue has been approved by the Central Political Conference and urgently needs to be implemented. Therefore, he came to Shanghai to consult with various circles in Shanghai to discuss ways to implement the blockade. (2) Regarding the abolition of the tael and adoption of the dollar issue, the first meeting of the Abolition of Tael and Adoption of the Dollar Research Committee the other day had achieved considerable results. Therefore, Song also needs to consult with the financial circles in Shanghai again. Therefore, he temporarily suspended his trip to Wuhan and came to Shanghai. After completing his official duties in Shanghai, he will return to Nanjing and then go to Wuhan.

Postal Administration's Handling of Mail from the Eastern Provinces 92

Official Announcement Yesterday

According to the Dagong News Agency, the Shanghai Postal Administration yesterday issued Bureau Order No. 1606, stipulating the handling of mail from the three northeastern provinces: In order to inform you, regarding the suspension of all postal services in the three northeastern provinces, as notified in Bureau Order No. 1602, now, according to the telegram from the Postal Administration, the following measures should be taken for mail to and from the three northeastern provinces. It is hereby ordered that all of you should comply with this order. The details are as follows:

Incoming Mail: (1) All incoming mail originating from the three northeastern provinces (except the South Manchurian Railway area) and transferred from Dalian or other places, bearing (a) counterfeit Manchurian postal stamps, (b) Japanese ordinary postal stamps, (c) Republic of China postal stamps canceled with the first year date stamp, will be regarded as not having paid postage. The mail will be collected with postage due. (2) All mail bearing uncanceled Republic of China postal stamps, or if the mail indeed originates from the Kwantung Leased Territory and bears Japanese postal stamps, will be regarded as having paid sufficient postage as usual. (3) All mail originating from the South Manchurian Railway area (except the Kwantung Leased Territory) bearing Japanese ordinary postal stamps will be regarded as having insufficient postage. However, only a single domestic postage fee needs to be paid.

Outgoing Mail: (1) Mail to the Kwantung Leased Territory will be transferred through Dalian as usual, and mail to Korea will be transferred through Dalian, Japan. (2) Mail to the Asian part of Russia will be transferred through direct ships via Shanghai and Vladivostok, and mail to the European part of Russia will be transferred via the Suez Canal or the Pacific Ocean. Unless further notified, Japan shall not be used as a transfer bureau for transferring other foreign mail sealed and sent by our country.

Postal Director Zha Peilin.

Methods for Sending Mail to Europe 93

Choose Ships Carefully: According to postal authorities, mail to European countries may be delivered via Canada, the United States, or the Suez Canal, unless further notice. The ships used for transport are carefully selected for their fastest sailing speed. The schedule for sealing and sending mail to European countries before August 8th is as follows:

Ship Name Sealing Date and Time Departure Date Estimated Arrival Date in London Number of Days Required

Empress of Canada July 31st, 11:00 PM August 1st August 28th 27 days

Conte Rosso August 5th, 8:00 AM August 5th August 30th 25 days

President Cleveland August 8th, 9:00 PM August 9th September 4th 26 days

Utilizing Aviation: According to local postal authorities, China Post has always been actively utilizing airmail services from southern China to Europe. Since the opening of the Saigon-Marseilles airmail route last year, China Post has entered into necessary arrangements with Indochina Post to utilize this newly opened air route for mail delivery. Mail to various landing places along the route can also be delivered at the same time. The place names are as follows: Bangkok (Siam), Yangon (Myanmar), Kolkata (British India), Karachi (British India), Dizak (Persia), Bhojak (Persia), Baghdad (Iraq), Beirut (Syria), Rhodes (Asia Minor), Athens (Greece), Naples (Italy), Marseilles (France).

The Saigon-Marseilles airmail route operates once a week, with landing points as mentioned above. All senders can use this route to send mail to these places. This is because these mails can be transferred from Hong Kong to Haiphong to connect with the special express train from Haiphong/Hanoi to Saigon. For transfer details and airmail rates, please inquire at all post offices and ask for forms for review.

In addition, whether the airmail route from Bandung (Java) to Amsterdam can be utilized and whether it can be transferred via Singapore is currently under negotiation.

Japanese Obstruct Postal Workers from Entering Customs 94

Japanese Residents Sent Mail Yesterday

According to the Guowen News Agency, Japan is actively undermining China's postal rights. After we implemented the blockade of postal services in the three northeastern provinces, the settlement of affairs in the three provinces is entirely handled by Ba Lidi, the postal director of Liaoning Province. The deputy postal director, Liu Yaoting, has already entered the customs and arrived in Shanghai to report to the General Administration about the various experiences and current situation of being seized. The information that the reporter inquired about from various parties yesterday is summarized as follows:

Japanese Obstruct Entry into Customs: The reporter inquired from the local postal authorities yesterday and learned that after the eastern provinces were ordered to be blockaded, all remaining affairs have been settled. All personnel, those who wished to leave left, and those who did not wish to enter customs also closed their doors and ceased operations, to show non-interaction. However, some personnel wishing to enter customs, feeling that transportation was difficult and blocked and aware of the dangers along the way, first asked Post Director Ba to issue passports to the Japanese consulate in advance to return to China via Dalian. However, the Japanese side initially agreed, but then, seeing that we had implemented the blockade, deliberately delayed the issuance of passports, causing some postal workers to be stranded in the eastern provinces, unable to leave. Although Post Director Ba of Liaoning Province tried to negotiate, the other party remained calm. It seems that this will create obstacles again. Yesterday, the post office received a telegram from Liaoning Province, also reporting the situation of being obstructed by passports.

Remarks by Zhu Menghou: The reporter met with Zhu Menghou, Director of the General Affairs Department of the Postal Administration. According to him, since the blockade of postal services in the eastern provinces, not only are letters not sent to the northeast, but also all post offices in the eastern provinces are closed. This is a step that we are forced to take. As for the takeover by the puppet state, this is what they obtained by force, and it is not that we asked them to take over because we suspended operations. All personnel, after the blockade order was issued, regardless of rank, from the postal director down to the postman, were free to enter customs if they wished, otherwise they were free to leave. Because we implemented the blockade, the puppet state sent personnel to seize the property by force on the 24th. Some personnel, because they are registered in various provinces inside the customs, wanted to enter the customs and return home, but due to passport issues, they are still staying in Shenyang. Therefore, Post Director Ba of Liaoning Province telegraphed today to report to the General Administration about this.

Lin Shi May Arrive This Morning: The rumor that Lin Shi, Director of the Postal Department of the Ministry of Communications, has arrived in Shanghai is not accurate. The reporter visited his residence yesterday and was told that Lin must take the overnight express train from Nanjing to Shanghai tonight (i.e., yesterday) and will arrive in port tomorrow morning (i.e., today). Not only will he consult with the puppet state's postal service, but also Lin must attend the Postal Economic Committee meeting on Friday (today).

Japanese Establish Postal Services in Tianjin and Qingdao: According to the Central News Agency, recent reports indicate that the Japanese have established counterfeit post offices in Tianjin and Qingdao and are sending mail, undermining China's postal system. The General Administration of Posts specially telegraphed the post offices in Tianjin and Qingdao yesterday morning to inquire in detail. If the reports are true, they will report to the Ministry of Communications and consult the Ministry of Foreign Affairs for serious negotiations. In addition, the property of the Liaoning, Jilin, and Heilongjiang Postal Districts, including real estate, totaling more than 2.9 million yuan, was seized by the rebels. Regarding the issue of postal remittances and savings in that area, according to Zhu Menghou, Director of the General Affairs Department of the Postal Administration, the rebels are naturally responsible for it.

Japanese Mail Sent to the Northeast Yesterday: The Japanese temporary post office at the Japan Club shipped a total of 169 bags of mail collected yesterday bound for Harbin and Siberia in the Northeast on the Dalian Maru. The mail was unloaded in Dalian. The ship passed Qingdao, and the Japanese in that port also received mail and sent it to the Northeast.

Northeast Customs Officials Come to Shanghai 95

According to the Far East News Agency, after the Northeast and Dalian Customs were seized by the Japanese-incited puppet state, all Chinese officials in the customs, feeling the unfavorable environment and Japanese threats, secretly packed their bags and left the customs. The first batch of over twenty people, including Ke Nahua, Chen Minglan, Chen Gengping, Huang Wenjie, and their families, arrived in Shanghai by ship from Dalian yesterday. It is reported that a second batch will arrive in Shanghai within days.
