The Blood Soul Eradication Corps Bombs the Yongchang Coal Company with a Hand Grenade 97

Business Partner Yu Ruiliang Injured

A group identifying themselves as the Blood Soul Eradication Corps previously placed hand grenades at the Cotton Fabric Industry Guild and the Gauze Exchange Broker Guild as warnings, as reported in yesterday's newspaper. Yesterday, an explosion occurred at the Yongchang Coal Company near Chihang Bridge.

Yongchang's Past

The Xin Sheng News Agency reports: Wu Jichang, the manager and owner of the Yongchang Hongji Coal Company at 729-731 Xin Zha Road, is considered a mid-sized enterprise in the coal industry, having been in operation for over twenty years. It employs twelve shop assistants and forty workers, and is a member of the Shanghai Coal Industry Guild. On January 19th of this year, the entire coal industry boycotted the patriotic movement due to the coal company's actions, colluding with the British firm, Mackinnon Mackenzie & Co., to falsely report to the police, leading to the arrest and investigation of Yan Bin. After a general meeting, a two-day strike was decided. Yan Bin was found not guilty by the court and released, and the company resumed operations. The Yongchang Coal Company was expelled from the guild and banned from operating in the market.

Bomb Explosion

At 7:45 AM yesterday, the coal company had already opened for business when a young man, about twenty years old, wearing a white short shirt and pants, was seen loitering in front of the shop carrying a paper package. He immediately unwrapped the package and forcefully threw it inside, then fled. A loud explosion occurred, and thick smoke filled the air. Shop assistant Yu Ruiliang, 27 years old, from Yuyao, Zhejiang, was immediately injured in the buttocks by the blast. Bleeding profusely, he collapsed in extreme pain. All the workers and shop assistants were terrified upon hearing the explosion.

Police Investigation

Manager Wu Jichang, who was upstairs at the time, heard the explosion and came downstairs. Upon seeing the situation, he immediately reported it to the Xin Zha Police Station by telephone. Six Chinese and foreign armed detectives were dispatched to investigate. They found that coal balls and wooden boards placed against the west wall of No. 731 had been blown into a hole. Three holes were found in the sunshade canvas. A bicycle was destroyed. A piece of fuse rope, about a foot long, was found and taken back to the police station for thorough investigation. The injured shop assistant Yu Ruiliang was taken to Renji Hospital for treatment. As the injuries were minor, he was bandaged up and discharged immediately. However, at 4:00 PM, the bleeding from his buttocks had not stopped, and he was taken back to Renji Hospital by the shop owner for further treatment.

Eradication Corps Letter

The coal company received a letter yesterday stating: "Wu Jichang of the Yongchang Coal Company, be informed that this morning's small gift was a special reward for your meritorious service in selling Japanese coal. You may continue to sell more in the future. Our group will give you a generous reward. This is a warning from the Shanghai Blood Soul Eradication Corps, July 28th." It is also reported that the Shanghai Municipal Council received a letter from the group stating: "To Whom It May Concern, Our group is entirely organized by Chinese patriotic volunteers with strict discipline. Our sole purpose is to eliminate treacherous merchants who sell Japanese goods. We will not cause any harm to the peace of this city. Please do not interfere with our future actions. With regards, The Shanghai Blood Soul Eradication Corps." It is also reported that the Cotton Fabric Guild and the Gauze Exchange also received a letter from the group stating: "To the Standing Committee of the Cotton Fabric Guild, We trust that you have received and understood our letter and small gift yesterday. We hereby issue a serious warning. Please immediately notify your members within three days and publish a large advertisement on the front page of major newspapers in this city, stating your determination not to sell Japanese goods. Otherwise, our group will consider that your guild has no sincerity in resisting enemy goods and will take serious action against you. With the country in dire straits, we are prepared to die for this cause. From the Shanghai Blood Soul Eradication Corps." The letter received by the Gauze Exchange was similar.

Accountant's Explanation

A reporter from the Xin Sheng News Agency met with the accountant of the coal company yesterday, who stated that the case involving the arrest of an investigator from Mackinnon Mackenzie & Co. in January had absolutely nothing to do with the coal company. As for the guild's expulsion of the company, the matter has not yet been resolved. This time, it was definitely a misunderstanding that the coal company was a traitor.

Japanese Goods Plummet in Price

After the Gauze Exchange Broker Guild and the Cotton Fabric Industry Guild received bomb warnings, the price of Chinese gauze in the Shanghai Gauze Exchange soared yesterday, while the price of Japanese gauze suddenly plummeted. Japanese cotton cloth in the cotton fabric market fell sharply, with few customers inquiring about it. The sales of domestic cotton cloth turned buoyant.

Cotton Industry Announcement

After receiving a warning from the Blood Soul Eradication Corps, the Cotton Fabric Industry Guild issued a special announcement yesterday stating: "For the matter of announcement, it was found that today (July 27th) at 11:30 AM, a young man in a Western suit delivered a letter and a tin can of biscuits to the guild and handed it to the tea server. The young man then turned and left. Upon opening it, it was discovered that the can contained a hand grenade, and the letter warned members not to traffic in enemy goods. We have reported this matter to the police and had the letter and hand grenade removed. We are now urgently copying the original letter and announcing it to the market, hoping that all members will pay close attention to avoid endangering themselves. This is what we earnestly hope. This announcement."

The Japanese Government Allocates Huge Sums to Revive Japanese Ships on the Yangtze River 98

Large Quantities of Japanese Goods Shipped Out Yesterday

Nisshin Steamship Company to Resume Regular Service

What Are the Thoughts of the Chinese People on This?

Japanese merchant ships on the Yangtze River have been suspended since the January 28th Incident, with only a few ships being leased to the Japanese Navy for transporting military supplies. After the Japanese troops withdrew, many Japanese bridges on the Yangtze River resumed operations. However, the Nisshin Steamship Company's riverboats have not yet officially sailed. Mr. Yoneri Monji, the president of the Nisshin Shanghai branch, went to Japan to discuss the plan to revive Yangtze River shipping with the head office and the Japanese government. The conclusion of the discussion was that, firstly, the anti-Japanese movement among the Chinese people must be fundamentally eliminated, and secondly, the government should allocate funds to support the company's resumption of shipping. It is now heard that the anti-Japanese issue has been raised by the Shanghai Japanese Residents' Affairs Committee, which has requested the Consul General in Shanghai to implement the conditions of the January 28th Agreement to stop anti-Japanese activities. Therefore, Japanese goods imported into Shanghai have begun to be shipped out in large quantities from yesterday. At the same time, with the government's financial assistance, the company's resumption of Yangtze River shipping will also be realized from August 1st. There will also be a plan to lower prices and reduce fares to compete with Chinese and foreign ships on the same route. The details of this matter are recorded below:

Dispatching Ships

The Nisshin Steamship Company originally had more than twenty ships on the Yangtze River route. All of them were suspended during the war. Later, the Daifuku Maru and others were leased to the Navy for transportation. Now, the company has recovered all the leased ships and temporarily assigned the Fengyang Maru, Xiangyang Maru, Nanyang Maru, and other ships to operate the Shanghai-Hankou regular service. The Xinyang Maru will operate between Yichang and Chongqing. The Luoyang Maru, Yueyang Maru, Ruiyang Maru, and other ships that have been suspended for a long time will be used to increase services when Japanese ships on the Yangtze River can transport Chinese goods and passengers. Currently, a few ships will be used for trial voyages. Japanese staff at various docks and branches along the Yangtze River, such as Hankou, Jiujiang, Wuhu, and Yichang, who were evacuated during the war, have now been reassigned to their positions.

Loading Cargo

A large amount of Japanese goods has been accumulated in the upper reaches of the Yangtze River. In addition, many Japanese goods have recently been transported from the East to Shanghai and then to Hankou and other ports. Starting on the 27th, the Japanese, disregarding the boycott and refusal to transport goods in the interior, openly declared and transported a large number of Japanese piece goods, foreign paper, kelp, groceries, etc., stored in Shanghai. The Fengyang Maru of the Nisshin Steamship Company was used for transportation. All customs declaration procedures were handled by the Japanese themselves. The first batch of a large amount of Eastern goods, about 10,000 pieces, was bound for various ports on the Yangtze River and left Shanghai yesterday morning. This is the largest first batch of Japanese goods transported to Hankou after the war. The Navy has been ordered to protect the loading and unloading of goods along the way.

Financial Assistance

The Nisshin Steamship Company has been suspended since February 1st, exactly half a year. The company has suffered huge losses in business. According to the company, the monthly loss is at least 150,000 to 200,000 yuan. Now, the company is urgently seeking to resume operations. Mr. Yoneri Monji, the president of Nisshin Steamship Company, requested a large subsidy from the Japanese government as funds for the revival of Japanese ships on the Yangtze River. It is now confirmed that the Japanese Ministry of Communications has decided to allocate 1.2 million Japanese yen for the revival of Yangtze River shipping, as the Yangtze River shipping is crucial to the sales of Japanese goods. It is said that the funds have been issued, and Nisshin will use them to restore riverboat services.

Price Cuts

The Japanese also know that it will not be easy to restore the Yangtze River shipping to its pre-war state. Japanese merchants have been discussing the plan to restore Yangtze River shipping in recent days. It is heard that they have decided to exploit the Chinese merchants' weakness of greed for profit, collude with treacherous merchants to solicit passengers and cargo, and secretly reduce the fares to half of the price set by the six companies. For passengers, a reduction plan will be set. For example, the first-class fare from Shanghai to Hankou is 50 yuan, but the Japanese ships will only charge 25 yuan. Second and third-class tickets will also only be half price. Steerage passengers will be allowed to ride for free with limited restrictions, only collecting a small ticket fee. The price will be increased when business improves. This move by the Japanese will also severely hit Chinese merchant ships. It is said that the Japanese government will subsidize the operating losses during the restoration period.

The Hurricane Will Not Come to Shanghai 99

It Will Make Landfall Near Xiamen

According to a report from the Xujiahui Observatory yesterday, the coast between Xiamen and Shantou is experiencing fierce winds and waves, and the weather is extremely bad. The center of the hurricane was located within 60 miles of the intersection of 213 degrees North Latitude and 117 degrees East Longitude at about 6:00 AM yesterday, and was moving slowly in a northwest direction. Based on the forecast of its direction, if there are no special changes in the weather, it is likely to make landfall near Xiamen.

The Shanghai Times reported that the heat has been severe for more than ten days, causing great distress to people. Hearing the news that a hurricane is approaching China, people suddenly had the hope that it might blow over Shanghai and wash away the heat. However, inquiries to the meteorological authorities yesterday revealed that the hurricane was passing through the Balintang Strait and moving in a northwest direction, completely unable to pass over Shanghai.

Incense Workers Strike Yesterday 100

Request for Improved Treatment Rejected

Labor Union Reports to Party and Government for Investigation

The Da Gong News Agency reports that more than 400 incense workers in this city suddenly went on strike yesterday due to repeated oppression from employers and difficult living conditions. The labor union has reported the situation to the Party and government agencies. The details are as follows:

Reasons for the Labor Dispute

The wages of incense workers are very low, and the workers have great difficulty making a living. The labor union convened a representative assembly in August last year, and representatives were sent to negotiate with the employers, requesting improved treatment. The employers repeatedly refused. Later, the Shanghai War broke out, and the negotiations were suspended. After the ceasefire agreement was signed and the situation stabilized, the labor union again sent representatives to negotiate with the employers, but to no avail. The Social Affairs Bureau convened labor and management representatives for questioning twice, but only the labor representatives attended, and no management representatives attended, resulting in a prolonged lack of resolution. Recently, the employers of various stores have successively fired more than 100 workers. Workers in the Nanshi and Zhabei districts had no choice but to go on strike voluntarily yesterday. After hearing the news, the labor union sent personnel to investigate everything and reported it to the Party and government agencies for investigation.

Demands

After the incense workers went on strike, they made four demands to the employers: (1) Employers shall not dismiss workers without reason. (2) Employers are required to pay the labor union 100 yuan per month for operating expenses. (3) Employers shall not use breaches of labor-management contracts as excuses. (4) Wages and various expenses shall be increased by 40% across the board.

Impact on the Concessions

After the incense workers' strike occurred, only workers in the Chinese-controlled areas inside and outside the city and in Zhabei participated in the strike yesterday morning. After hearing the news, workers in the concessions also joined the strike in the afternoon, and the situation is quite serious.

Wang Chongzhi Defends the Mackay Communications Contract 101

Declares That He Has Always Opposed It and Did Not Participate

Requests That the Machine Purchase Contract and Attachments Be Announced

Chen Fumu, the Acting Director of the Ministry of Transportation, was attacked by outsiders regarding the communications contract signed between the Ministry of Transportation and the American Mackay Company. In his statement published in the newspapers, he implicated Li Fanyi, the former Director of the Department of Electrical Administration of the Ministry of Transportation, and Wang Chongzhi, the Director of the International Telegraph Bureau. Subsequently, Li and Wang resigned. Wang also sent a letter to Huang Shaoxiong, the Acting Minister of Transportation, and sent a special letter to Chen Fumu after his resignation to defend himself. The original letter is as follows: Mr. Fumu, With respect, I read your statement on the Mackay Communications Contract in various newspapers on July 17th. There are many points that do not conform to the facts and insult others. Due to my official position, I have remained silent to await a fair judgment from society. However, the Shen Bao published a letter from Mr. Zhenru to Mr. Jikuan on the 21st, saying that Wang Chongzhi violated discipline and should be punished. I am extremely confused and horrified. However, right and wrong can never be subdued by power, and interests can never be concealed by false words. Now that I have resigned, I would like to state the following to you:

Opposing the Contract

(1) I have always expressed my opposition to the Mackay Communications Contract. I first telegraphed you in mid-February, saying: "To Chen, Acting Director of the Ministry of Transportation in Nanjing, I have received your secret telegram. I have investigated that there are many disputes over China's international radio communication loans, including the Sino-Japanese Shuangqiao Radio Station, the Sino-American United Contract, the Sino-British Northwest Three Stations, etc. All these contracts allow others to have exclusive rights. When the Ministry of Transportation and the Construction Committee planned to set up a large international radio station, they all purchased equipment with cash and operated it independently to avoid causing diplomatic problems. When the Zhenru Grand Radio Station officially reported, Japan protested that it infringed the interests of the Shuangqiao Radio Station. This is one point. The Ministry of Transportation and the Construction Committee previously signed communications contracts with the United States, Germany, France, and the Philippines. Now a certain American company is willing to invest in setting up a station for China, which is for the purpose of communications contracts. This point conflicts with the current Sino-American communications contract. This is the second point. The equipment prices of the International Grand Radio Station are not too high, and the revenue from reporting fees is huge. Domestic banks and the Postal Savings Bureau may also be willing to invest in purchasing equipment. This is the third point. My bureau has two powerful Fenbao 2-kilowatt transmitters that have not yet been installed. During Minister Wang's term, it was planned to increase the power to 20 kilowatts for global communication, with a budget of 300,000 yuan, which could build two large radio stations. This is the fourth point. However, this matter is very important. I have briefly stated one or two points based on my limited understanding. I respectfully ask for your instructions. Signed, Wang Chongzhi." Finally, on June 28th, upon hearing that the contract was about to be signed, I telegraphed Director Li to express my opposition, saying: "Urgent, To Director Li of the Ministry of Transportation in Nanjing, Secret, I heard that the Mackay Communications Contract is about to be signed. This matter will be subject to arbitration in the future, and our side will inevitably lose. It will not only damage the country's reputation but also harm the Minister's reputation. Chinese electrical personnel are completely speculative. Why be fooled? I intend to telegram the Minister to ask him to reconsider. Sincerely, Zhi." It can be seen that those who supported the signing were others, and it was definitely not me.

Did Not Participate

(2) When the Sino-American communications contract and the machine purchase contract were signed, Mr. Sun Sheng, the assistant manager of the China Electric Company, was also present. After the two contracts were signed, Mr. Zhenru gave the Minister a copy of the China Electric Company's proposal for the Mackay Contract and wireless telephone. At the same time, Mr. Sun requested the Minister to give specific instructions. He did not say anything about signing. At that time, the Minister asked Director Li what his opinion was. Director Li said that Article 11 of the Joint Venture Company Communications Contract states that "Both parties are free to sign wireless radio communication contracts with other countries, but they shall not violate the provisions of Articles 2 and 3 of this contract." "Other countries" seem to refer to countries other than the parties involved. If Mackay, an American company, signs another contract, it may be contradictory. He suggested that legal experts should review it to avoid repeating the mistake of losing the Czechoslovakian arbitration and harming the country's reputation. Regarding the telephones, he said that technical issues should be handed over to wireless electrical engineers for detailed review. The Minister said yes. These were the facts at the time. The section of the above-mentioned four contracts that you mentioned on the table is definitely not true, as anyone who has experienced it knows. As for the section where the Mackay Company supplemented the responsible guarantee letter, saying that I also praised it as extremely appropriate, national administration cannot be interfered with by a company, and national reputation cannot be guaranteed by a company. Anyone with common sense should know this. Although I am foolish, I have never expressed support for this kind of proposition.

Signed Hastily

(3) According to your statement, the Mackay Communications Contract and the Wireless Telephone Machine Purchase Contract were signed on June 27th. However, Director Li did not submit his resignation until the 29th, and the acting person during his sick leave was Zheng, the section chief of the first section of the Department of Electrical Administration. Therefore, the Department of Electrical Administration was never without a responsible person, and the exercise of power was never interrupted. May I ask why the two contracts were signed hastily without being submitted for detailed review beforehand, and without being countersigned afterwards? Also, why was the machine purchase contract not reviewed by the engineers in charge of the International Radio Station? Why was it purchased hastily and not announced? (4) On June 28th, Chen Hezong, the secretary, showed me a draft of the Mackay Communications Contract. (I only saw the original Communications Contract in the newspaper, and I never saw the Machine Purchase Contract). Although this is true, I immediately stated that I fundamentally disagreed with the contract. Even in terms of wording, there were inappropriate places. I pointed out several places and telegraphed Director Li to oppose it on the same day. I did not expect that it would be signed without going through the Department of Electrical Administration. As for your statement that the contract was "brought to the Ministry for sealing, and other than the two copies left in the Ministry, it was handed over to the company for safekeeping," there were no witnesses on the Ministry's side, so how could it be handed over to the company? And whether the sealing of the contract was on June 27th or on the morning of July 6th (the date of Director Li's handover), the rumors are different, and there is no way to know the details. Furthermore, the Mackay Contract (and its attachments, i.e., the guarantee letter) should be announced in full.

Collaboration with the Puppet State

(5) Regarding the American joint venture company's communication with the puppet state of Manchuria, I have repeatedly reported to the Ministry to ask for instructions on how to deal with it. At the same time, the Ministry also telegraphed Director Zhang of the Beiping office, who originally signed the Northeast-American communication contract, to negotiate with the company, and consulted the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to negotiate with the American government. Recently, Section Chief Zheng has repeatedly urged Director Liu of the European and American Department of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to handle it quickly. Therefore, I cannot be solely responsible for the delay. Furthermore, I telegraphed the Ministry on April and June to ask for instructions on the negotiation policy, but I did not receive a reply. You were acting as Minister at that time, so you are actually responsible for the delay. Furthermore, we believe that the American company's communication with the puppet state of Manchuria violates the provisions of Articles 2 and 3 of the Ministry's contract. The American company believes that it is continuing the old Northeast contract and is not violating the contract. According to Article 10 of the contract, any disagreement in the interpretation of the contract clauses should be submitted to arbitration. However, because the Northeast contract conflicts with the Ministry's current contract, and the Ministry has never denied it, and our country is also communicating with the three northeastern provinces, we may not necessarily win if we submit it to arbitration. Therefore, we first started with diplomacy. As an insider, how can you deny that you are unaware of the complicated situation in this matter? Is the termination of communication and the signing of the Mackay Contract in violation of the original contract? Is it deliberately causing disputes?

Unfair Machine Purchase

(6) You said that the price of the Marconi machine is 50,000 US dollars more expensive than that of the China Electric Company. I don't know on what basis. I have investigated that the bidding for the two large radio station components was opened publicly by five companies: Siemens, the French Long-Distance Telephone Company, the American Joint Venture Company, the China Electric Company, and the Marconi Company. The China Electric Company quoted 138,000 US dollars, and the Marconi Company quoted 42,000 pounds (plus three items: amplitude modulator, broadcast machine, and vacuum tubes, about 4,000 pounds), which is about 148,000 US dollars, about 10,000 US dollars more expensive. But the components are different, and it is not easy to compare. You said that you agreed to sign the communications contract, but agreed to open bidding for the machine purchase, as if these were two unrelated matters. Are you completely unaware that the Ministry of Transportation borrowed British Boxer Indemnity funds to purchase machines, and that the success or failure of the Sino-British communications contract was a condition for the machine purchase? In fact, the draft has been approved by you, and the case has been approved by the Executive Yuan. It is not something that can be changed by empty words. As for your proposal to purchase five telephones worth more than 300,000 US dollars, which was never quoted to various businesses, it seems to be inconsistent with your proposal to purchase through open bidding. As for whether these telephones are needed in China at present and whether the Ministry of Transportation has the financial resources, these are obvious facts and do not need to be repeated.

Loss of Sovereignty

(7) Regarding my personal situation, one statement is that "Wang Chongzhi has a close relationship with the company (American joint venture company), so he deliberately delayed the negotiations." Another statement is that "It is heard that this statement was made by Wang Chongzhi at the instigation of the American joint venture company." May I ask what the meaning of "close relationship" is, and what is the evidence of "instigation"? Please make a clear statement. I am a self-respecting person. How can I be "suddenly slandered"? (8) Article 11 of the Mackay Communications Contract states that the company may use the designated route to solicit business for transmission. This matter was strongly contested by the Water Line Company during the Water Line negotiations in the past. We firmly rejected it on the grounds of sovereignty. Now we are lightly granting it to the Mackay Company. If the Water Line Company demands the same treatment in the future, who will be responsible for the loss of rights? Furthermore, the communications contract states that "Wireless radio direct communication circuits have been established between the United States and Cuba, Colombia, Peru, and Argentina, which can be connected to the Ministry's radio stations for commercial reporting." The intention seems to be to control our country's future communication rights with various South American countries. I cannot help but be extremely worried. (9) Regarding the fact that Chinese and foreign countries have recently published the Wan Guo Telegraph and Telephone Public Affairs Contract, you accused me of intentionally slandering. This is impossible. On the 8th of this month, because I saw that the news published in the Dalu News was not completely true, I published a statement, intending to correct the news. There was not a single word attacking you. The facts are all there. Can you show people the evidence of slandering you?

Worthy of Attention

(1) The Shishi Xinbao published a Reuters New York dispatch on July 24, saying: "Mackay Wireless Telegraph Company announced today that the Chinese National Government has granted the company the concession right to operate Chinese telephone and telegraph..." The significance of this dispatch is very great, and I think you are also deeply aware of it. If it is true, then your claims of breaking the monopoly and abolishing unequal treaties are just a sham. I hope you will announce all the contracts and documents as soon as possible to dispel public doubts. In short, I have always prioritized the cause of serving the country. I deeply hate the actions of foreigners who use huge profits to lure me to achieve their secret control of our country's communication sovereignty. This time, seeing the waste of national funds in wireless telephones and the introduction of wolves into the house and the Mackay contract causing disputes and being self-defeating, I forgot my own humble position and repeatedly expressed my humble opinions to fulfill my national duty. My views have always been inconsistent, and it is natural to attract jealousy. Right and wrong will be left to future generations. Because your statement repeatedly mentioned my name, I have now resigned from the position of Director of the International Telegraph Bureau, so I dare to briefly state one or two things and ask for your scrutiny.

Facilities for Navigation Administration on the Yangtze River 102

Among wheel-powered vessel transportation, the most important thing is navigation markers. Transportation prioritizes safety, and markers are crucial for avoiding danger. All countries meticulously research maritime affairs, carefully planning for every contingency. China has also been progressively setting up such markers along its coast and rivers. However, the Yangtze River's course is ever-changing, requiring even greater caution. The administration of navigation markers in our country has long been handled by the Customs Service. In the 31st year of the Guangxu reign (1905), the Customs Service established the River Inspection Department, specifically responsible for Yangtze River markers. The overall situation of this endeavor is worth mentioning. Our newspaper has specially investigated and briefly recorded it below, so that those interested in navigation affairs may have a reference.

The Customs Service's involvement in navigation markers stemmed from the treaty ports agreement, which included provisions for setting up lighthouses along the coast to indicate navigation routes, with arrangements to be discussed by consular officials and trade ministers. At that time, China considered the Customs Service to be an agency established by the Chinese government. Furthermore, few Chinese people were proficient in applying scientific technology. Therefore, the task was entrusted to the Customs Service. Initially, the number of personnel was small, as the quantity of markers depended on the river's conditions and navigation traffic. As navigation increased, more markers were added. Over the past thirty years, the personnel employed by the Customs Service in this area are roughly as follows:

Upper Yangtze:

In the 2nd year of the Republic (1913), there were 2 foreign staff and 34 Chinese lighthouse signal personnel. By the 20th year of the Republic (1931), there were 3 foreign staff, 3 Chinese office staff, and 58 lighthouse signal personnel.

Lower Yangtze:

In the 26th year of the Guangxu reign (1900), there were 15 small steamer crew members and 80 lighthouse keepers. In the 2nd year of the Xuantong reign (1910), there were 1 foreign technical specialist, 1 ordinary sailor, 1 Chinese draftsman, 31 small steamer crew members, and 57 lighthouse keepers. In the 9th year of the Republic (1920), there were 5 foreign specialists, 3 ordinary foreign staff, 2 Chinese river affairs clerks, 2 draftsmen, 28 waterway management sampan sailors, 47 small steamer crew members, and 204 lighthouse keepers. In the 19th year of the Republic (1930), there were 15 foreign specialists, 3 Chinese river affairs assistants, 6 clerks, 6 draftsmen, 7 waterway inspectors, 15 repair and miscellaneous staff, 125 small steamer crew members, 242 lighthouse keepers, and 5 water level table recorders. By the 20th year of the Republic (1931), there were 16 foreign specialists (4 on leave), 3 Chinese river affairs assistants, 6 clerks, 6 draftsmen, 8 inspectors, 15 repair staff, 127 small steamer crew members, 288 lighthouse keepers, 52 lighthouse keeper sailors, and 5 recorders. The extent of this rapid growth is evident.

The increase in markers installed over the past thirty years is as follows:

(Upper Yangtze) Xuantong 2nd year Republic 9th year Republic 19th year

Signal Stations 4 20 37

Sampans 1 4

Marker Ships None None 12

Piles 1 4

Water Levels 2 10 77

Shore Marker Flags None None 32

Water Marker Flags 13 13 14

(Middle Yangtze) Xuantong 2nd year Republic 9th year Republic 20th year

Piles 13 20 312

Lightships None 3 2

Marker Ships None None 10

Buoys 26 29 36

Bamboo Buoys Established as needed

Signal Stations None None 2

Survey Sampans 7 9 12

(Lower Yangtze) Guangxu 26th year Xuantong 2nd year Republic 9th year Republic 20th year

Piles 29 39 48 97

Lightships 11 26 44 43

Marker Ships None None 2 3

Buoys 5 3 2 7

Bamboo Buoys Established as needed

The advancement of navigation due to these markers is self-evident. In the middle and upper Yangtze, the draft limit before the 12th year of the Republic (1923) was a minimum of 5 feet and a maximum of 9 feet. Now, it is a minimum of 6.5 feet and a maximum of 22 feet. As a result, ships with a draft of 18 feet can now directly reach Shashi. The draft limit for downstream steamers has also increased. For example, the cargo weight in shallow water and normal times has increased from 180 tons to 1,500 tons. The number of steamship voyages on the upper Yangtze was only 10 in the 3rd year of the Republic (1914), with 100 voyages throughout the year. In the 19th year of the Republic (1930), there were 65 steamships, with 1,149 voyages throughout the year. This is due to the installation of markers, which allows navigation even during shallow water periods. With the increase in navigation frequency and cargo volume, national tax revenue has also increased accordingly. At various Yangtze River ports, the total tonnage of steamships in the 26th year of the Guangxu reign (1900) was 31,582,370 tons, while in the 19th year of the Republic (1930), it was 51,738,671 tons, an increase of 20,56,301 tons. The cargo value in the 26th year of the Guangxu reign (1900) was 190,602,138 taels of customs silver, while in the 19th year of the Republic (1930), it was 561,001,804 taels, an increase of 370,399,666 taels. Tax revenue in the 26th year of the Guangxu reign (1900) was 5,913,247 taels of customs silver, while in the 19th year of the Republic (1930), it was 15,621,710 taels, an increase of 9,708,463 taels. These are substantial figures, demonstrating the importance of markers.

Navigation is not limited to markers alone. Mapping is also essential. The Customs Service's River Inspection Department surveyed 27.5 miles from the 32nd year of the Guangxu reign (1906) to the 2nd year of the Xuantong reign (1910), 248.0 miles from the 1st year of the Republic (1912) to the 9th year of the Republic (1920), 5,386.9 miles from the 10th year of the Republic (1921) to the 19th year of the Republic (1930), and 569.3 miles in the 20th year of the Republic (1931). The mapping process is complex. In the 20th year of the Republic (1931), there were 141 resurveys, covering a linear distance of 538 miles. Furthermore, there is the International Lighthouse and Buoy Unification Conference, held in Lisbon in the 19th year of the Republic (1930), which was attended by representatives from the Customs Administration to improve mapping. Besides markers, the piloting of ships themselves is also something that those involved in navigation administration should pay attention to. Yangtze River piloting is divided into three sections: from Shanghai to Hankou is the first section, from Hankou to Yichang is the second section, and from Yichang to Chongqing is the third section. The first section has a pilot association with 31 Chinese, 1 Westerner, and 1 Japanese pilot. There are only 10 Chinese pilots. The second section has no pilot organization; ships are free to hire pilots. The third section has 150 Chinese pilots, managed entirely by the Customs Service in accordance with pilot regulations.

Due to the various necessary facilities such as markers in navigation administration, there must be funding. Those who bear this cost, for the convenience of wheel-powered vessel transportation, collect it from ship cargo taxes, called "ship tax." The ship tax is taken from merchants and designated for specific use. The shortfall is subsidized by the Customs Service, which is also included in the Customs Service's budget. This is an agency that generates profit, aiming to facilitate commerce, eliminate danger, and increase tax revenue, rather than simply a tax-collecting agency that relies on ship tax for income.

China has been managing Yangtze River navigation administration for decades, with the Customs Service's River Inspection Department responsible. The achievements are as described above. It is our belief that the Yangtze River is the sole key to transportation in central China. Before the completion of roads such as the Sichuan-Hankou, Ningxia-Hunan, and Ningxia-Hankou routes, all passenger and cargo transport relied on it. It is hoped that government officials and merchants will pay special attention, allowing the Customs Service to continue its management, achieving greater and newer results from its experience. In the near term, this concerns the safety of navigation administration; in the long term, it concerns national tax revenue, all of which are of utmost importance and cannot be ignored.

Case of Intercourse Between Humans and Dogs 103

From March to June,

Performances almost everywhere in major hotels,

Four girls looked haggard,

Trial opened yesterday, spectators barred.

Based on a tip, police officers Tang Jian, a Chinese detective, and Bart, a Western detective, from the Xinzha Police Station raided No. 12, Hongfu Lane, Xinzha Road, and uncovered a setup where humans and dogs engaged in intercourse. The main culprits, Chen Xinzhai and Liu Xinshan, and Chen's mistress, Ms. Lu, were arrested, along with a black dog and four girls: Chen Shuanglin, Chen Guilin, Caiyun, and Genling. They were all brought to the First Special District Court for interrogation. The details of the human-dog intercourse have been reported in our newspaper. The police investigation revealed that Chen Xinzhai and his wife repeatedly took Shuanglin and the other three girls and the black dog to Rooms 119 and 115 of the Oriental Hotel on Zhejiang Road, Room 217 of the Da Zhonghua Hotel on Xizang Road, Room 205 of the Central Hotel on Guangdong Road, and Room 217 of the Shenzhou Hotel on Zhejiang Road between March and June this year to perform these inhumane acts of human-dog sexual intercourse. Each performance required at least ten viewers, and each person had to pay five dollars. Therefore, they earned at least fifty dollars per performance. Liu Xinshan also assisted Mr. and Mrs. Chen in committing these criminal acts. The four girls were sent to Guangren Hospital, where it was confirmed that their lower bodies had been damaged. The black dog was also sent to a dog examination center. On the 26th and 27th of this month, Chinese and Western detectives took the four girls to the various hotels to reenact the performances, some on beds, some on sofas, etc. Yesterday morning, Magistrate Wu Tingqi continued the trial of the case in the Second Criminal Court. The black dog and the four girls were brought to the court, and more than a hundred people were in attendance, mostly women. Police lawyer Wang Yaotang requested that spectators be barred from the courtroom, citing the case's impact on public morals. The court granted the request. The spectators, who had come full of excitement, left disappointed. After the spectators left, police lawyer Wang rose and stated that the prosecution was in accordance with Articles 241 and 257 of the Criminal Code. He then detailed the detectives' reenactment of the performances at the hotels with the children. The defendants had rented Room 115 at the Oriental Hotel for a month, from April 11th to May 11th. They later rented Rooms 116 and 119 for a considerable period. Overall, the duration was extremely long. These performances also took place in Rooms 115 and 119, making it difficult for the hotel staff not to be aware of the situation, suggesting that they had assisted in the obscene acts. The court then examined the hotel registration book, confirmed its accuracy, and questioned the staff on duty. Subsequently, the four girls were brought before the court. Caiyun and Genling were only five years old and had just been weaned. Therefore, one was held in the arms of a Jiliang Institute worker, while the other sat on the lawyer's bench, allowing the magistrate to question them up close. The two girls looked particularly haggard. Shuanglin and Guilin stood before the lawyer's bench, with Shuanglin doing most of the answering, as the eleven-year-old was more mentally capable than the five-year-olds. After Shuanglin recounted the entire situation, Mr. and Mrs. Chen still tried to deny it. The court then ordered the black dog to be brought out. The dog, about a foot long and covered in black fur, immediately rushed toward the four girls, displaying various aggressive behaviors. Representatives from the four hotels then filed a report, stating that they were unaware of such events. Chen Shuanglin also submitted a petition detailing the training for human-dog intercourse, claiming that in addition to Mr. and Mrs. Chen, there was also a "Old Seven" (who is now on the run). Chen Xinzhai's face was full of smoke and his spirits were low, suggesting that he had been suffering from withdrawal for many days. However, his mistress, Chen Lu, was fat and had a well-fed appearance. Her responses were also quite fluent. Therefore, she firmly denied all accusations, claiming that they were framed by the mistress of "Old Seven," who had a grudge against them. They hired lawyer Gan Lin to defend them. Lawyer Gan asked the court to question the four girls about whether they had taken off their clothes during the performances. When Shuanglin was asked, she replied that they had not. The police lawyer then stated that the suspects often had the victims wear "split pants" during the performances, and that the victims could be asked again. When Shuanglin was asked again, she confirmed that they did wear "split pants," indicating that this aspect was irrelevant. Subsequently, Magistrate Wu adjourned the case for another hearing and ordered the four girls to be examined by a forensic doctor.

Roulette Gambling Den Uncovered on Route Ghisi 104

Undercover detectives pose as gamblers,

A large quantity of gambling paraphernalia confiscated.

The French Concession police have recently been conducting strict investigations and crackdowns on prohibited activities such as opium and gambling within the concession. They learned that a Westerner had been running a large private roulette gambling den at No. 809, Route Ghisi, with tens of thousands of dollars changing hands, in violation of the prohibition order. At 10 PM the night before, Western Detective Chief Xia Cai'er, along with Western Detectives He Licai, Ge Lai'er, Da Ershang, Chinese Detective Inspector Shen Defu, Chief Detective He Tugeng, Deputy Detective Liu Kunbao, and undercover detectives Dai Rongji, Zhang Wenliang, Kong Qingtong, Bai Xiuhui, etc., traveled in separate cars, quietly and without raising suspicion, to conduct a raid. The location was spacious, with gardens and open spaces surrounding it, covering an area of over thirty mu. The gambling den was deep inside, with people stationed around to keep watch, making it difficult to raid. Therefore, the Western Detective Chief instructed the detectives to disguise themselves as gamblers and enter one by one. When the gamblers were in the midst of their excitement, the detectives gave a signal and surrounded the area, arresting on the spot Russian Bai Xigao Fu, Chinese Wang Mengwan, Zhao Jinhua, Li Fangsheng, Li Ayou, Chen Xiaoliang, Shen Jinzhang, Wang Fubao, Lu Dahai, Gao Zhenfu, Chen Jiande, Wang Baoren, Pan Dong, Xu Xuesheng, Shi Wencai, Luo Yupei, Zhu Quancai, Zhang Yutang, Liu Wenjin, Xu Xuehou, Jiang Shasi, Qiao Xiaomao, Wu Xingong, Yao Zhiliang, Yuan Chunfang, Wang Juhai, and a woman named Xia Wangshi, totaling twenty-seven men and women. Confiscated gambling paraphernalia included a roulette wheel, two table cloths, twenty-two boxes of chips (approximately three thousand pieces), three dice, as well as five sets of opium smoking paraphernalia, including attachments, opium sticks, opium boxes, and ledgers. All were taken to the police station. After interrogation, seven gamblers were released on bail of thirty dollars each, pending further instructions. The remaining suspects were detained. Labor Dispute Resolved at Lao Gong Mao Shipyard 105

Laid-off workers to be rehired or compensated,

Workers' savings to be fully refunded.

The entire workforce of the Lao Gong Mao Shipyard in Pudong went on strike due to the management's harsh treatment and violation of labor contracts, leading to a serious labor dispute. The Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs, fearing escalation and impact on local security, convened a mediation session at 9:00 AM yesterday. Chen Yisheng and Xu Wanli from Lao Gong Mao Shipyard, and Lu Yunqing and Wu Shaolin from the Fifth District Shipyard Workers' Union, attended. The session was chaired by Wang Bing, Director of the Mediation Division of the Bureau of Social Affairs, and recorded by Wang Zhiqin. After lengthy discussions, both parties reached an agreement and signed a resolution: (1) Apprentices Chen Huifang, Chen Defeng, Xu Aliang, Zhao Jingui, Zhu Tusheng, and Zhao Yougen will resume work immediately. Workers Yuan Amao, Zhong Agen, Kang Zhangquan, Wang Shunkui, Gao Asi, and Xi Zhaogen will terminate their employment relationship with the shipyard. (2) The workers whose employment is terminated will be paid severance pay and wages for one and a half months by the shipyard. (3) Workers employed by the shipyard may not board or lodge outside the shipyard without the shipyard's permission. The shipyard must provide meals with the same variety of dishes as before, deducting seven dollars per month for meals. (4) Workers who do not eat at the shipyard this month will not have their meal expenses deducted. (5) All previously deducted savings will be refunded.

One policeman shot in the waist, life in danger.

At 9:40 PM last night, police officer Sun Jiming from the Liyuan Road sub-station of the Second District was patrolling the intersection of Xieqiao Liyuan Road and Xinjiao Road, carrying a Mauser pistol with the number 71326. Suddenly, three robbers appeared from the north. One was wearing a black silk shirt and pants with slippers, and the other two were wearing blue cloth shorts and shirts. One of the robbers, wearing a blue cloth shirt, grabbed patrolman Sun Jiming around the waist. The robber wearing the black silk shirt and pants fired a shot, hitting the officer in the left leg. The officer immediately fell to the ground, and the robbers snatched the Mauser pistol. The wounded officer, still conscious, blew his whistle to alert others. The two wounded police officers were taken to Shanghai Hospital by the sub-station's vehicle for treatment. It was reported that the officer shot in the waist was in critical condition.

Report on Disaster Relief in Wuhu 110

A Tragic Story of Selling His Wife to Save His Family

The Shanghai Chinese and Foreign Relief Society at No. 12, Renji Road, is aware that the spring drought in Anhui Province is particularly severe. In addition to the counties of Xuancheng, Wuwei, and Nanling, which have already been allocated large sums of relief funds, the suffering of farmers in various villages in Wuhu is even more tragic. Yesterday, another 10,000 yuan was allocated and sent to the Wuhu branch for distribution. The following is an excerpt from the disaster relief diary reported by the special disaster relief commissioner of the branch, which reveals the plight of those who have been forced to sell their wives to save their daughters: "On July 2nd, when distributing relief in Huanjia Village, we met a man named Huan Zengyou. This man is over sixty years old and is known for his honesty and selflessness. He has four sons (the eldest son died early), four daughters-in-law, six grandsons, two granddaughters, and two granddaughters-in-law. It can be said that he is blessed with a large family. However, since the severe flooding last year, there has been no harvest, and the family's livelihood has been disrupted. By this spring, they could no longer sustain themselves. The third son, Shouzhong, who is educated and knows propriety, has always been filial and respectful. Seeing that there was no rice left in the house and no way to borrow money, he was willing to sacrifice the love and affection between husband and wife and sell his twenty-five-year-old wife to another man for ninety yuan to save the lives of his family of more than ten people. It is said that before Shouzhong sold his wife, the brothers had an important meeting and all proposed drawing lots to sell a wife to save the whole family. However, Shouzhong did not agree with this idea, saying that his eldest sister-in-law was a widow with four children, his second sister-in-law also had many children, and his fourth sister-in-law had not even been married for a year. If they drew lots and chose one of the eldest sister-in-law, the second sister-in-law, or the fourth sister-in-law, wouldn't that be a sin for my third brother? Regardless, they should not be sold. Furthermore, I cannot allow my brothers to sell their wives to support my useless couple. It is better to sell my wife, which is more appropriate. After Shouzhong said this, the brothers all shed tears and cried bitterly. As a result, it was decided to sell Shouzhong's wife. When Shouzhong's wife learned of this, she cried and begged her husband to go out and beg for food to support his father. Shouzhong told her that this would not save the whole family and tearfully tried to persuade her. His wife could not be persuaded and knelt down and cried. On the day before their separation, she could not eat and sobbed uncontrollably. The scene was unbearable. Later, it was said that his wife cried all day long at her new husband's home, thinking about Shouzhong. Shouzhong's actions are truly admirable and worthy of respect. His wife's sorrowful separation can be described as tragic. Seeing the situation, we felt pity and sought economic assistance from all parties, hoping to redeem Shouzhong's wife and reunite them, bringing happiness to the whole family. Upon hearing this story, all of you must feel sympathy and want to help restore this true love. Therefore, we have recorded it in detail after returning home."

Merger of Ho Fung and Two Other Banks 113

Capital and Government Bonds Totaling 25 Million Yuan

Ho Fung Bank received a telegram yesterday from its Singapore headquarters stating that Ho Fung Bank, Overseas Chinese Bank, and China Merchants Bank have decided to merge. Ho Fung, Overseas Chinese, and China Merchants Banks were all founded by overseas Chinese in Southeast Asia, with headquarters in Singapore. They are large in scale and have established credit. Ho Fung has a capital of 4 million Singapore dollars, Overseas Chinese has 5.25 million Singapore dollars, and China Merchants has 1 million Singapore dollars. After the merger, their paid-up capital and public reserve funds will reach 12 million Singapore dollars. Calculated at the current exchange rate, this is equivalent to approximately 25 million Chinese yuan. Among the banks operated by Chinese in our country, it will be one of the most substantial.

Shanghai Municipal Council Temporarily Increases Number of Russian Members in Volunteer Corps 115

During the martial law period this year, the Russian division of the Shanghai Municipal Council Volunteer Corps recruited additional personnel. After discussion by the Shanghai Municipal Council Preparedness Committee, it was deemed that these corps members had received training, and if financially feasible, a portion could be retained. Subsequently, the Board of Directors consulted the Finance Committee on the matter. After careful consideration, the committee recommended that the Board of Directors approve the retention of 73 of these Russian members for the remainder of the year. However, the financial situation should be reviewed again at the end of the year, and this should not be taken as a precedent for increasing the number of Russian members or increasing expenses after 1933. This recommendation was adopted by the Board of Directors this past Wednesday.

Orphanage Completes Reunion 116

You Sha Travels 5,000 Li to Find Daughter

Gu Youdao Celebrates Obtaining a Jewel

The Shanghai Tzu Er Jiao Yang Yuan (Orphanage), affiliated with the Chinese National Child Welfare Association, rescued a kidnapped maidservant named You Xialan in April of the 19th year of the Republic (1930). When the girl was kidnapped, she was only six years old. She only knew that her father's name was You Sha Wu and that he lived near Jing Tou in Yang Kou, Changshan, making tofu for a living. She knew nothing else. The Tzu Er Jiao Yang Yuan initially sent people to Changshan County, Zhejiang Province, to investigate. Then, after carefully examining the girl's accent, they found it was similar to that of Jiangxi. Upon checking postal routes, they discovered a place called Yang Kou in Guangfeng County, Jiangxi Province. The orphanage immediately sent a letter to the county government requesting an investigation. Later, they received a letter from You Sha Wu claiming that Xialan was indeed his daughter and had been kidnapped three years earlier. Upon learning of the whereabouts, the orphanage sent a letter urging him to come and claim her. Coincidentally, Gu Youdao, a resident of Beixin Jing, had no children and wanted to adopt a daughter to ease his loneliness. He and his wife visited the orphanage, and they fell in love with Xialan at first sight. They immediately requested to adopt her. The orphanage declined the request because Xialan had a father. After a few days, You Sha Wu indeed traveled thousands of miles to Shanghai. Father and daughter met, their joy and sorrow indescribable. However, You Sha Wu's family was very poor. His intention this time was just to see her, not to take her home. Now that he learned that the Gu family loved this girl and that the girl also wanted to stay with them, he readily agreed to the arrangement. From then on, the two families would be relatives, and the poor girl would have found her place. The orphanage went to Changshan in Zhejiang and then to Guangfeng in Jiangxi to search for the girl's family. They finally found her biological father, allowing the family to reunite. Their meticulous efforts are commendable.

Report on Cholera by the Seaport Quarantine Office 117

Wu Liande, Director of the Seaport Quarantine Office and Director of the Central Cholera Prevention Bureau, released the ninth cholera report yesterday (the 27th), as follows: (1) Cholera in Shanghai has clearly reached its peak. As of the end of the week of July 23rd, a total of 411 new cases were discovered during the past week, with 36 deaths. A breakdown by area is listed below:

Area Cases Deaths

Shanghai City 82 9 (1 foreign national)

International Settlement 266 (8 foreign nationals) 24 (2 foreign nationals)

French Concession 31 (2 foreign nationals) 2

Unspecified Areas 32 1

Total Last Week 411 (11 foreign nationals) 36 (5 foreign nationals)

Total Previously 1655 (24 foreign nationals) 98 (8 foreign nationals)

Total as of Last Weekend 2066 (35 foreign nationals)

134 Deaths (11 foreign nationals). (2) According to the weekly report of the Health Department of the Shanghai Municipal Council, the total number of cholera patients was 617, which is 206 more. However, the above numbers were not based on bacteriological examination. Subsequently, the authorities of the Health Examination Office of the Shanghai Municipal Council and the Shanghai Municipal Health Laboratory declared that approximately 30% of the stool samples examined were positive. The examination procedures included (a) culture, (b) indole reaction, and (c) serum agglutination reaction. (3) Of the above numbers, the number of foreign cholera patients last week was 11, which is higher than before. However, the mortality rate for this cholera outbreak in Shanghai is still the lowest, only 6.4%. (4) The current cholera outbreak seems to be related to the climate. The previous 8th report reported that the temperature had reached 101.1 degrees Fahrenheit, with a humidity of 95 degrees. However, the highest temperature in the shade last week was 100.9 degrees, with an average of 90.6 degrees, and an average humidity of 80.2 degrees. (5) The cholera epidemic is widespread in the country this year, reaching Guangzhou in the south and Changchun in the north. Its ferocity is similar to that of tropical areas such as Siam and Annam. Until last year, it was almost an annual scourge. Also, the Calcutta area of India (population 1.5 million) reports approximately 150 cholera patients per week, with a mortality rate of 40% to 50%. Bombay, however, has not been affected. (6) The results of cholera prevention in various cholera-affected areas in the country this year are good. In my opinion, there are three main reasons: (a) Regarding the health authorities: 1. Careful preparation to supply safe drinking water; 2. Strict control of vegetable markets, restaurants, cold drink shops, and other public places; 3. Control of food vendors and others related to food shops; 4. Cholera vaccination for citizens; 5. Organization of bacteriological examination offices; 6. Strict implementation of seaport quarantine, isolation, and other epidemic prevention measures. (b) Regarding all sectors of society: 1. Assisting health organizations in implementing cholera prevention measures; 2. Urging health authorities to improve all necessary defenses; 3. Establishing charitable organizations and promoting high-level knowledge among the public; 4. Conducting joint research on good methods during non-epidemic periods to prevent the recurrence of epidemics. (c) Regarding individuals: 1. Each individual using new methods to protect the safety of their family; 2. Using health and hospitals to prevent and treat the disease; 3. Using the power of charity to help the poor and needy. (7) The Shandong ship departed from Shanghai for Shantou on July 19. Because a helmsman suddenly contracted cholera, it returned to the port on the evening of the same day. The quarantine officer went to the ship at 4 a.m. the next morning to quarantine it, vaccinated all crew members and passengers against cholera, and sent the patient to the Shanghai Epidemic Hospital on Xizang Road for treatment. His life could only be extended by three days. Although the dangerous symptoms disappeared, he eventually died of uremia. This was because the person had a smoking habit, which led to kidney failure. (8) Passengers traveling from Xiamen and Shantou to Malaya, the Dutch East Indies, Siam, and the Philippines must be vaccinated against cholera before leaving port. The same applies to those traveling from Shanghai to Qingdao, Java, and Luzon.

Shanghai Cotton Yarn Exchange Bans Private Spot Trading Within the Exchange 119

The Shanghai Chinese Cotton Yarn Exchange's brokers' cotton yarn futures trading has always used Shenxin Factory's Zhong brand cotton yarn as the standard. Substitutes are also limited to those listed in the grade table. The exchange recently received reports of private spot trading occurring. It specifically posted the following notice in the market hall the other day:

The subject matter of trading in this exchange is specified separately in the exchange's cotton yarn and cotton grade table. Cotton yarn and cotton that are not listed in the grade table, regardless of the method adopted, may not be traded in the exchange's market. In addition, spot trading was originally within the scope of the exchange's business. Although the exchange currently only holds futures trading, it has not abandoned the franchise for spot trading and should be protected by law. Recently, it has been heard that some people are privately doing spot trading in the exchange's rest area. The type of subject matter is unknown. These messages have been reported by outsiders and do not seem to be completely unfounded. If this behavior does exist, it not only violates the Exchange Law and the exchange's operating rules but also infringes upon the exchange's franchise for spot trading and should be subject to legal sanctions. In addition to sending a separate letter to the Brokers Association for thorough investigation, the joint notice is hereby issued, hoping that all brokers will assist the exchange in unanimously banning this illegal behavior to respect the law and prevent malpractices. Your cooperation is highly anticipated.

Page 12

Photographic Reproduction of the Song Dynasty Qisha Tripitaka 123

The translation and publication of Buddhist scriptures in China initially only had handwritten copies. Later, there were stone carvings, and then wood carvings. With the advancement of printing, circulation became more convenient and widespread. This flourished during the Song Dynasty. The Shu version of the Northern Song Dynasty, the Eastern Chan Temple version of Fuzhou, the Kaiyuan Temple version of Fuzhou in the Southern Song Dynasty, the Wang Yong Cong version of Sixi, the Zifu Temple version of Sixi, and the Yansheng Temple version of Qisha were all renowned among versions. However, today, to see their relics, the Shu version is as rare as a phoenix, and even the five versions after the Eastern Chan version have only a few fragments or later supplementary versions that are not original prints in domestic and foreign collections. Now, the Qisha Tripitaka reproduced in Shanghai is complete and is the original print, which is extremely rare. The planning of the Qisha Tripitaka began during the Duanping era of Emperor Lizong of the Song Dynasty (1272 AD). Biqiu Zizhi Hong of the Yansheng Temple in Qisha, Pingjiang Prefecture, vowed to amputate his arm and raise funds to publish the complete collection of sutras, precepts, and treatises. It was completed during the reign of Emperor Shizu of the Yuan Dynasty. The original was in the form of a Sanskrit scroll. The collections of the Wolong and Kaiyuan Temples in Xi'an are now preserved by the Shaanxi Provincial Library. Zhu Qing Lan discovered them last year while distributing relief. Each block has five pages, each page has six lines, and each line has seventeen characters. There are Jiaxi (1273 AD) and Chunyou (1281 AD) era names. Ye Gong Chuo, Jiang Wei Qiao, Di Bao Xian, Xu Nai Chang, Ding Fu Bao, Wu Zhao Zeng, Li Jing Wei, and others all believe that the Dharma repository, which has been submerged for a long time, has encountered an opportunity to flourish. It will make many contributions to world culture and art. They discussed reproducing and distributing it. The Shanghai Song Edition Tripitaka Reproduction Association was organized to be responsible for the reproduction. All distribution matters were entrusted to the Buddhist Studies Bookstore. They were responsible for compiling and checking the scriptures, collecting missing chapters, ordering printing paper, and selecting and hiring teachers, preparing glass plates, and going to Shaanxi for photography. After experiencing various difficulties, they have achieved considerable success. It is estimated that 500 copies will be reproduced, each with more than 6,000 volumes, and books will be published in installments. It will take two years to complete the publication. Pre-orders are priced at 525 yuan. A notice will be published in the newspaper soon. The reporter has seen the original scriptures. The calligraphy is ancient and elegant, the engraving is exquisite, and there are very few errors or omissions. The Buddhist images carved at the beginning of the volumes are especially solemn and beautiful. The calligraphers and engravers of the time made vows and signed their names, which contained merit, which is different from other books that are done for profit and perfunctorily. To study, recite, and collate it, it is truly possible to clarify the obstacles of later editions. Libraries and academics will likely rush to order it.

Embezzlement Case of Manager of Textiles Store 125

Judge Reprimands Defendant's Base Behavior

Zhou Jinhua, a local man who was the manager of the Yu Feng Yuan Foreign Goods Textiles Store at 578 East Xihua De Road, was accused of embezzling more than 17,000 yuan of capital by forging deposit slips with fraudulent means between January and June of this year and fleeing. The general manager, Zhou Xiong Cai, reported the matter to the Huishan Police Department, which dispatched Chinese and foreign detectives to arrest Zhou Jinhua and escort him to the First Special District Court. It was found that the amount of the virtual deposits in the account books was quite inconsistent. The defendant was ordered to pay 20,000 yuan in substantial shop security, and an accountant was instructed to thoroughly check the accounts. This has already been recorded in this newspaper. Yesterday morning, Judge Fu Lin continued the trial in the Fourth Criminal Court. According to the plaintiff's attorney, Lu Qi, during the adjournment, accountant Zhao found that the prices of the goods and pieces ordered by the defendant with various foreign firms were not stated, and there were many malpractices. The deposits of more than ten households, including the Chun Ji household, were completely fabricated. Subsequently, the plaintiff Zhou Xiong Cai testified that the funds handled by the defendant were all unreliable. Accountant Zhao Zuwei also provided a certificate. When questioned by Zhou Jinhua, his statements were evasive, saying that the prices of the goods ordered with various foreign firms were based on pounds and shillings, and all the depositors were not fabricated and that they all existed. The court announced that during the previous trial, the deposit of Yuchangxiang Foreign Goods Store was testified to be false by the store's manager, Zhou, who was a member of the same clan as you. Your behavior is clearly base. The court then ordered the case to be adjourned for further verification. The defendant was still released on the original bail.

Employees' Union: Gao Jinkun, Song Yaoqing, Cheng Yuliang, and others from the Organizing Committee of the Shanghai Special Municipality Labor Occupational Union Organizing Committee, had previously submitted to the Public Training Committee of the Shanghai Special Municipal Party Department, indicating that before the central government promulgated new regulations on public organization organizations, if a formal public organization had not yet been established, its establishment should be temporarily delayed. Dock Workers: The Shanghai Dock Workers Promoting the Implementation of the 28 System Committee declared, "For the Reference of All Sectors of Society: We, the dock workers, rely on our flesh and blood year-round, braving the wind and dew, toiling under the scorching sun in the summer and wading through ice and snow in the winter. Our lives are lighter than chickens and dogs, and our labor exceeds that of cattle and horses, but the wages we receive are extremely low. Individual sustenance is insufficient, let alone family life. Therefore, the lives of our dock workers are the most miserable among the working masses. Moreover, there are labor contractors who exploit us, squeezing our lifeblood. Of the fixed wages, the workers only actually receive 20-30%, while the contractors take 70-80%. These contractors gain without labor, reaping huge profits, and are able to paint rafters and carve beams, with courtyards full of wives and concubines, wearing fine clothes and eating rich food, with horse-drawn carriages racing, treating our 70,000 workers as slaves, while they sit proudly as southern-facing kings. This kind of feudal contracting system, from the standpoint of the interests of our workers themselves and from the standpoint of humanitarian justice, has absolutely no reason to exist. Moreover, the abolition of the contracting system is clearly stated in the Party's program. Therefore, under the rule of the current National Government, this contracting system has no possibility of being preserved. Previously, the Central Government, taking into account the actual situation, did not decisively implement the abolition, but on December 24, 1928, convened three representatives each from labor and contracting parties and formulated six principles. Our workers have always supported the Central Government's intentions and accepted them all immediately. However, the contracting party has resisted implementing the third principle: 'The contracting system is still temporarily allowed to exist, but the amount of the contractor's deduction of contract money shall not exceed 20% of the total amount, and the worker shall receive 80%. The allocation of import and export surcharges shall be temporarily based on the 28 ratio. The Suzhou Creek surcharge shall still be based on its old customs.' For more than three years now, the contracting party has refused to fulfill this principle. In this age of material civilization, the cost of living increases year by year, and the price of everything in Shanghai is even higher than in other cities. The wages that our workers earn with blood and sweat are forcibly exploited, making it impossible for them to sustain themselves. The hardships of the past few years can no longer be tolerated. Therefore, last month, we submitted a petition to the central Party and government authorities, requesting the implementation of the previous case. Now, having understood the suffering of the workers, the central Party headquarters and the Ministry of Industry have each sent special commissioners to Shanghai and have consulted with the Party and government agencies in this city to assist in handling the matter. At present, all of our dock workers in the city are holding onto great hope, quietly waiting for the authorities to handle the matter. If the contracting party stubbornly clings to its private views and refuses to implement the 28 system, then all of our workers will take effective measures to negotiate with the contracting party, and we will not stop until we achieve our goal. We hope that all sectors of society will understand the suffering of the lives of our dock workers and provide strong assistance, for which we will be endlessly grateful. This is our declaration."

Weather Report 140

Faculty and Students of Jinan University Petition for the Abolition of Colleges 145

Faculty and students of Jinan University in Shanghai, regarding the abolition of the College of Law and the College of Education, divided into four groups (current students, the Shanghai Alumni Association, the Overseas Chinese Student Union, and the Professors' Association), totaling about 20 representatives, have been in Beijing since the 25th, petitioning in various directions. On the morning of the 27th, Wang Wei, Ping Zuren, Wei Zhenhua, and others, representatives of the Alumni Association, went to the Ministry of Education to petition. Secretary Gao Tingzi received the representatives and stated the reasons for requesting the withdrawal of the order to abolish the colleges. The reasons were: (1) Jinan is the highest institution of higher learning for overseas Chinese, so education focuses on overseas Chinese. Jinan has a well-equipped law school that can train overseas Chinese diplomatic talents. (2) Jinan University is a whole national education institution. The College of Education studies the customs of overseas Chinese land temples, using the power of education to improve them, so that overseas Chinese can stand on an equal footing and develop the industry and commerce of Southeast Asia through the power of education. (3) Overseas Chinese have donated funds and made various contributions to the government. It seems inappropriate not to help expand the only overseas Chinese Jinan University in Shanghai, and to abolish it. Moreover, this matter was not discussed with the school authorities in advance, so the school has already hired many professors. It is difficult to reverse the contract with the professors due to the sudden abolition of the school, which is extremely difficult in practice. Secretary Gao said that the government has a whole plan for this matter, and the Ministry of Education cannot provide relief, only promising to convey the representatives' intentions to the vice ministers. Although the representatives still requested to see the vice ministers, they did not get what they wanted.

Draft of Last Year's National Track and Field Championships' Highest Records by the National Sports Advancement Association 159

Drafted new records distributed to various regional advancement associations and major sports meets for verification

The National Sports Advancement Association, in order to review and determine the national track and field highest records for the 20th year, drafted several new records and distributed them on December 23rd of last year to various regional advancement associations and major sports meets for verification and confirmation, so that they could be formally reviewed and approved by the board of directors. However, due to the impact of the national crisis, no definite feedback has been received from the various associations to date, resulting in a standstill. It is now learned that the association has reprinted the draft records to urge the various regional sports associations to promptly verify the validity of the achievements in their respective regions, in the hope that they can be formally reviewed and announced by mid-September of this year. Attached is the association's letter to the various regional sports associations:

Respectfully, regarding the review and determination of the 20th year national men's and women's track and field records, we have specially sent you a copy of the draft new records for the 20th year men's and women's track and field events, requesting your association to review whether the records in your region are appropriate and provide formal certification. If there are other better achievements that have not been included, please supplement them so that this association can review and determine them accordingly. It has been more than half a year since this request was made, and we have not received a reply. We are now enclosing two more copies of the aforementioned draft records, and we hope that your association will comply with the previous letter and reply promptly by mid-September for formal review. This is our earnest hope. Sincerely, China National Sports Advancement Association, July 27th, 21st year.
