Page 13

Free Talk

Excerpts from Ninety-Three-Year-Old Ma Xiangbo

Innate Intelligence 160

—

The poison of the emperor's ideology in our common people can be said to be deeply rooted. I still remember that during the Xianfeng era, there was a Chongming licentiate who went to the palace examination for re-examination. The meaning of this re-examination was to check whether there was any cheating. The examination question was: "With intention, striking the chime?"! As a result of the examination, the licentiate was greatly favored by the emperor, and Xianfeng issued an edict that "this writing shall be the eternal law."

At that time, I heard the teacher say this to me, and I was very puzzled in my heart. I boldly asked the teacher:

"Does Xianfeng himself understand the eight-legged essay? How can he know that this article should be the eternal law?"

My teacher, upon hearing this, repeatedly shook his head, extremely frightened, and rebuked me: "The Son of Heaven is born with innate intelligence, how can you, a young man, talk nonsense?" This shows that at that time, no one dared to say a bad word about the emperor. The greater the emperor's power, the deeper the nation's laziness.

If based on the principle of "those with virtue have authority," Confucius should have become the emperor long ago. However, Confucius could only be an uncrowned king, and later generations only called him the "plain king." As for the emperor, he was born with innate intelligence, a "naturally born Confucius." Our people, poisoned by this emperorism, would have no new ideas or new knowledge. The common people were all frightened, and everyone lived in terror. Who would have the courage to create? Therefore, even Chinese rebellions had to rely on gods and ghosts, saying that they were acting on heaven's behalf.

In fact, the emperors of China's past dynasties were very naive. Qin Shi Huang can be regarded as an enlightened ruler, and he had the idea of reform. He was even able to achieve the major policy of changing the feudal system to a system of prefectures and counties. However, he eventually built the Great Wall, wanting to shut out the Xiongnu from thousands of miles away and close the door to rest easy! He only wanted to be a closed-door emperor, and did not want to be a king of the world who expanded his territory.

Cooling Powder 161

— Qian Taisheng

Summer is suitable for taking something cooling. However, Rehe is tense again. It is an extremely hot stimulant.

When the Nineteenth Route Army resisted, it happened to be a time of flying rain and snow, severe cold and freezing. At a time when water dripped into beads, they did not need to hide in the trenches and drink the cold wind. From the extremely low temperature that froze their limbs and the starving soldiers' lives, they had to pick up their guns and charge in the rain and snow. Just hiding next to a raging fire, listening to the news reports on the radio, even in the depths of winter, it was still warm and comfortable.

But now, in weather that is heating up to over 100 degrees, the Northeast heroes are in the fiery sand, under the scorching sun that can make people faint and suffocate, and in the rain of bullets like a storm, using the battle of their lives to win the glory of the nation. Although it is a fiery battlefield, the more enemies they can kill, the more it is like taking a dose of cooling powder.

It is reported that more than 3,000 enemy troops from Heilongjiang were riding in a train passing through Gaolingzi, when the National Salvation Army used three freight cars, which were placed in advance on the top of the mountain. When the train arrived, these three freight cars rolled down the hillside, instantly smashing seven sections in the middle of the dozen or so train cars. At the same time, the gunpowder in the cars exploded, and more than 400 people died under these freight cars and gunpowder. This kind of method of killing the enemy is just like taking a dose of extremely cold cooling powder in the summer. But we cannot deny that the people of Shanghai are only able to seek comfort. Under the modern era, there is no shortage of fragrant and palatable cooling powders. Facing the Japanese army's stimulant for coveting Rehe, at least it is like the Northeast, seeing it sink into decline in recent years and gradually regarding it as nothing. How can people believe that we can have a day to turn things around?

Jade Pendant Ring: On the morning of June 23rd, I woke up unable to complete my dream, thinking of Su Qu's birthday tomorrow. I sadly composed this poem and inscribed it on a ten-foot-wide painting of white lotus painted by Great Thousand Layman, depicting sleeping old mandarin ducks who do not marry. I also recorded Tianchi's verse in the painting. – Yu Cen

The moon falls in the guest's courtyard, and I am startled awake at my pillow. The powder-white dress is like jade, not yet cold is the autumn river. I do not trust the stars, they seem like tears hard to gather. Old feelings want to tease, suing to the hairpin, fearing the single boat lightly leaving, originally wrong. Bearing the graceful opening on the river, sleeping old mandarin ducks, people alone still recall the pleated skirt of Liu Xian. Early west wind secretly warns, Lingbo's eyes are clear, the water chestnut blossoms. A dream, light dust, dim years are like a hub, stubborn silk lotus root, exhausted heart, lotus bitter. Redeeming the calamity, the withered fragrance is all thin. Giving Wei Lang today's heartfelt feelings, not worth the slightly furrowed brow of the moth.

Old People Are Not Necessarily Without Vigor 162

— Wang Yu

Many say that old people have a sense of twilight and are not worth discussing with about killing enemies and saving the country. In fact, this is not always the case. The difference between twilight and vigor cannot be judged solely by age. Today's decadent youth, who spend their days indulging in the theaters and dance halls, pursuing love and making sexual pursuits their second life, are truly shrouded in twilight and are even less worthy of discussing killing enemies and saving the country with. Zhang Zhongren's desire to form an army of old men, full of ambition, is like General Lian still able to eat heartily and Ma Fubo going out to sit in the saddle again. Although he has not truly formed an army, it is still an expression of being full of vigor. And what I have heard of the Hunanese Ren Fuli even sees Zhang as being more vigorous. Old people cannot be generalized. Fuli is seventy years old, a former Hanlin scholar of the Qing Dynasty, who once served as a censor. He is strong in character and known for his outspokenness. During the Sino-Japanese War of 1894-1895, he was angered by Japan's brutality and requested to go to the front lines, spending several days amidst the smoke and bullets. However, the Qing army eventually collapsed, and there was no way to save the situation. Soon after, he submitted a memorial opposing something, greatly offending Empress Dowager Cixi, and was dismissed and returned to his hometown. He often lamented that foreign insults came frequently and that national affairs were deteriorating. Who would have thought that Japan would become more and more oppressive, even more brutal than before, and would even occupy our three northeastern provinces with force for no reason? Upon hearing this news, Fuli cried bitterly and said, "I never imagined that in my dying years, I would again witness the fragmentation of our land." He also said to his son, "I am old and my death is not regrettable, but I am unwilling for my children to be slaves of a conquered nation, eking out a living in the hands of foreigners. I should fight the Japanese devils with all my might. If the government implements the recovery of our land by force, I will definitely change into military uniform and go to fight the enemy, even as a common soldier, I would be willing." But waiting for a long time, the government had no intention of sending troops and spent his days writing in the air in frustration, almost abandoning food and sleep. He then drafted a petition, strongly arguing that it was necessary to send troops. It was a voluminous work of ten thousand words, and he personally traveled to Beijing to present it to the authorities. His son tried his best to dissuade him and offered to submit it on behalf of his father, but he would not listen. Alas, how can such a person be said to be old and have a sense of twilight?

Overseas Talk 163

— Huang Ren

The Original Site of Adam's Paradise – Sussex County, England. Although it is often praised in articles and sung in poems by general literary figures and writers, no one dares to say that this beautiful county with its beautiful scenery is the original site of the Garden of Eden for Adam and Eve, the ancestors of mankind. This is what American research experts have researched with a lot of thought and believe to be certain. According to him, most of the prehistoric relics found in archaeological or scientific records are not real. Only Adam, the first real man, the ancestor of mankind, actually lived in Sussex County. According to his research, it was about 1.25 million years ago. At that time, the world had not yet been developed, and of course, there were thickets and thorns everywhere. And roaming among these thickets and thorns were completely ferocious and terrifying mammoths and tigers and leopards with teeth like blades. Adam dodged east and west to save his life, and it probably took a lot of effort, just like us modern people living in the city, busy dodging cars on the streets.

The King of Fresh Fruit Industry in England – Forty years ago, there was an eleven-year-old poor boy in England who asked his father for three pennies, not to buy snacks or candy, but to buy twelve bunches of primroses. That night he sold them on the street for one penny each, earning a total of nine pennies. He was so happy that he thought about how to make money on plants from then on. Once, he got a few pea seeds and planted them in his small garden. More than a year later, he got thousands of pea seedlings, which he sold all together. At the age of fourteen, he engaged in the fresh fruit industry. At the age of seventeen, he opened a large fresh fruit store in Eversham and actually started doing big business. By the age of nineteen, he was the general manager of a large fresh fruit company. He also got the title of "King of Gooseberries" (because gooseberries are a kind of fresh fruit). He could export 114 tons of gooseberries every day, breaking the record in the fresh fruit industry. Who is this person? It is the current Chairman and General Manager of the National Canned Food Company, Mr. S. Smedley, who has 3,000 employees under his command.

National Products Factories Worth Introducing (13) 164

— He Gongxing

(1) (2) Machine-Made Paper Box Factory

Paper boxes are necessary for packaging commercial goods. In Shanghai, there are more than a thousand machine-made paper box factories, because they require little capital, have large sales, and are easy to set up. The larger ones include Zhou Tongxing on Sanyang Road, Mao Taixiang on Lao Beimen, Wang Juxing and Wu Jinxing on Baoxing Road, and others in the Hongkou area. There were also several large Japanese factories in the past in areas such as Yalv Road. After our people resisted Japan, they closed down one after another.

The rise and fall of box factories depends on the business operations of the customers they attract. If they attract soap factories, sock factories, food factories, etc., then the development of the box factory can be expected. However, in recent times, large factories, aware of the outflow of profits, often manufacture their own, such as the Yonghe Family and other factories. Only Mao Taixiang and Lianxing currently produce boxes with printing.

Box-making machines include two types: paper-cutting machines and stringing machines. Paper-cutting machines vary depending on the type of paper being cut, so the cutting knives are also different. Stringing machines mark yellow cardboard with knife marks along the lines, making it easier to fold and paste. Each paper-cutting machine costs more than 30 yuan, and each stringing machine costs around 120 yuan. The Hexing Machine Factory on Qipu Road in Shanghai is the most famous manufacturer.

Box-making raw materials include yellow cardboard, cardboard, crepe paper, etc. Yellow cardboard is mostly domestic, such as Golden Bear brand, Phoenix brand, etc. Cardboard is a Western product. Crepe paper used to be a Japanese product, but recently it has mostly been replaced by American products, but the price is more expensive.

Each machine can produce about 2,000 soap and sock boxes per day. The expensive boxes can cost more than one yuan each, while the cheap ones cost only three yuan per thousand.

The situation is very different when it comes to manufacturing cigarette boxes. The factory can manufacture large paper cigarette boxes with 50 or 25 packs. As for small cigarette boxes with 10 sticks, not only are the machines and work procedures different, but also it is impossible to set up a factory without 10,000 to 20,000 yuan.

Records of Knocking on the Bell in an Old Temple (58)

— Bu Chu Ting Cao Zhaifu

Sixty-Five

The Annual Plan for Children in the Old Temple is the annual plan for every child in the Old Temple, and it can also be said to be the annual plan for all the children in the Old Temple. The matters listed in the plan are the matters that every child does. If every child implements the plan accordingly, then the sum of individual achievements will become the overall achievement.

The matters listed in the plan are the minimum limits. Children with greater abilities can do more things or do each thing more. In case the ability is not enough, even the minimum limit cannot be done, there should be a flexible solution after review.

This plan is a trial draft. Because it is the first time to set this plan, everyone does not have sufficient experience and it cannot be set very correctly. Some amounts may be set too high, and some amounts may be set too low. We can try it out while recording the shortcomings to revise this year's plan or reset next year's plan as a reference.

The plan is set for people: people are not born for the plan. If the plan does not work, or if it is forced to implement it is harmful to life, we can propose amendments. We would rather sacrifice the plan for the sake of the child, and never sacrifice the child for the sake of the plan. However, the plan is set by everyone, and amendments must be passed by everyone. If an individual feels that there are shortcomings in the plan, they can propose it to the public for discussion, and they must not act arbitrarily.

Daily life such as eating and sleeping does not need to be reminded every day, so it is not included in the plan. Things that need to be improved in daily life such as bathing, drinking soy milk, etc. are emphasized in the plan. Everyone cannot help but doubt drinking soy milk, right? I will tell you: "Milky white soy milk is better than ginseng soup: drink it into your stomach, it is refreshing and healthy." If you don't believe it, try it. When these new things become natural habits, we don't have to include them in the plan anymore.

One particularly important point in this plan is cooperation. You see that growing vegetables, planting trees, building roads, exterminating pests, teaching others to learn, and earning money to support the Northeast all use the power of the public to create public achievements. Although the achievement of one person is small, if accumulated, it will naturally be spectacular.

Since we set this plan, we have increasingly felt that schools and society must be integrated to generate great power. When we discussed it, we found that there were many things to do in the village, but primary school students could only do a part. Can that part of the thing be put aside? If it is put aside, even the lives of children cannot be healthy. I won't say anything else, just say one thing. The people of the Old Temple drink dirty water, and even this dirty water is not enough to drink. If we want every child to grow plump and wash clean, and hundreds of herbs and thousands of flowers to flourish like children, then we have to dig several large wells. Digging wells is the first major event in running a school, but the work of digging wells is definitely beyond the capabilities of children. There are many such things. We have already made up our minds not to let individuals escape the net of life education. Since the children's strength is not enough to do this kind of work, Mr. Zhu thought of the young farmers. Young farmers are going to turn the countryside into paradise and turn hell into paradise. You are leading the way in front of the children with this mission.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Essay

To Resist or Not to Resist? 182

— Fo

Yesterday's newspapers contained two pieces of news that were quite confusing, and I would like to bring them up as follows:

(1) According to a report from Tianjin, on the morning of the 27th, the Japanese army stationed in Tianjin sent four freight cars loaded with 100,000 sandbags, electrical grids, wireless radio equipment, and military pigeons to Yuguan via the Beining Railway. Furthermore, according to a telegram, the Japanese have recently been deploying military forces along the (puppet) Fengshan Railway with extreme secrecy.

(2) According to a Reuter's dispatch from Peiping on the 27th, the authorities here deny the rumors circulating in Shenyang and Shanghai that Zhang Xueliang's troops are advancing from Jehol and gathering on the Manchurian border. They claim that Zhang's troops have not moved, and these rumors are completely unfounded.

Currently, the Japanese are making very active preparations for aggressive actions, yet the Peiping authorities are desperately denying any movement. How pathetic and deplorable is this? However, according to a friend, Zhang Xueliang's attitude has recently undergone a major change. He keeps proclaiming that he will resist to the death. If that is the case, then why are the reports about Zhang's troops advancing towards Jehol being denied?

It seems that Little Zhang's strategy has indeed changed. In the past, his advocacy of non-resistance was widely condemned by the world. So now, he has undergone a complete transformation into a proponent of resistance. Fortunately, he can continue to resist in words while remaining inactive, and he will no longer be criticized by the world. But the world will again criticize him for remaining inactive despite advocating resistance. He can then mobilize his troops a little, or dig a few trenches, which can be considered a defensive effort. This can also be considered resistance.

Therefore, there are two types of resistance: resistance in words and form, and resistance in strength and spirit. I wonder which type of resistance Zhang is adopting? As the saying goes, "At first, when I judge a person, I listen to their words and trust their actions. Now, when I judge a person, I listen to their words and observe their actions." Because there are so many slippery characters these days, who are often insincere and make empty promises. Their words are unreliable. I need to open my eyes wide and see what they are really up to!

Science

Chromium 185

— Zhong Hong

Formula: Cr Molecular Weight: 52

Chromium is a bright, crystalline metal that remains unaffected at ordinary temperatures. It does not dissolve even in an oxyhydrogen flame, but turns into a liquid when exposed to an electric arc. This metal is also very difficult to analyze, requiring heating to about 3,000 degrees before it starts to dissolve. In high-temperature air, it burns brilliantly. It also has four valences: II, III, VI, and VII. If its valence is II, then it is a base former. If its valence is III, then it is a strong base former. If its valence is VI, then it is an acid former. If its valence is VII, then it is a strong acid former. Even strong oxidizing nitric acid and aqua regia do not cause significant changes or reactions. However, sulfuric acid and hydrochloric acid can dissolve it, releasing hydrogen gas and leaving behind a chromium-containing salt.

Generally, alloys composed of highly reactive metals and those that are very resistant to corrosion often contain chromium. For example, when iron is mixed with chromium, it becomes a type of incredibly hard steel. Twelve to fourteen percent chromium, also known as stainless steel, is very hard and durable for making knives. The so-called stainless knives sold in the market are made of this.

When combined with nickel, it can be used to make steel helmets, armor, military uniforms, and shields that can withstand bullets. During the January 28th Incident, many brave soldiers of my 19th Route Army sacrificed their lives due to the lack of such protective equipment, while many Japanese soldiers survived because their helmets protected their heads. How tragic! The lack of scientific knowledge among the Chinese has reached this point. Alas, chromic oxide is used in paints and never fades. Chromic sulfide is excellent for tanning leather. The ancient method required eight months to tan a hide, but now it only takes four hours, and the results are several times better. Therefore, it has become an important material in modern industry and is also used as a mordant. Several acidic chromium compounds can also be used as pigments. As for the method of making chromium, there are three types:

1. Goldschmidt Process: Reduction of chromic oxide with aluminum.

2. Burning a mixture of charcoal and chromic oxide in a lime pot.

3. Reduction with zinc.

Chromium does not exist in nature in a pure state, but is contained in several compounds, such as FeOCr2O3. Its main production areas are in California and other places.

In short, chromium has long attracted the attention of the world (except China) and is of great help in warfare and industry. I hope readers will pay special attention so that I won't have wasted my time and effort in writing this.

Society Improvement Discussion Group

A Discussion on Improving Gift-Giving Customs 186

— Yixing

The principle of "reciprocity" in gift-giving is essentially an expression of human sentiments. As the saying goes, "Human feelings are like accounts to be settled." Therefore, simplicity and avoiding extravagance and novelty were the norm. The customs seemed to be fixed. However, in recent times, social morals have declined, and human relationships have become cold. Consequently, gift-giving has also changed significantly, often emphasizing hypocrisy, leading to people being burdened by the obligations of human relationships. This is especially prevalent in official circles, where the practice has become deeply ingrained. When superiors encounter weddings, funerals, or birthdays, their subordinates and colleagues engage in lavish displays of flattery, going to extremes. It's not uncommon for them to offer hundreds or thousands of gold coins for birthdays. Those with limited finances scrape together what they can. This results in monthly salaries being insufficient to cover the cost of gift-giving, leading to rampant corruption!

Furthermore, consider the ordinary exchange of gifts among people. They are often based on a person's status and reputation, regardless of the depth of their relationship. If you are a person of influence, even casual acquaintances will give generous gifts, hoping to curry favor. Even local bullies and village leaders exploit this, constantly inventing occasions like "yangshou" or "yinshou" every year, using them as pretexts to collect gifts, silver, and goods. Those with more prestige can even engage in outright extortion, making considerable gains. Customs have reached this point, and the abuses are endless. People have long wanted to speak out. Now that this local supplement has established a Society Improvement Discussion Group, I would like to contribute this issue for discussion. I believe that the following improvements should be made to gift-giving customs:

(1) Regardless of the wedding, funeral, or celebratory occasion, the maximum amount of money given as a gift should not exceed two yuan.

(2) When giving gifts, they should be practical items, limited in quantity and not extravagant.

(3) In the case of a funeral, if one has already attended the service and personally paid respects, there is no need to send anything else. Paying personal respects is a far greater expression of sentiment than any material gift. If one still wishes to honor the deceased, they can spend a few cents to write a eulogy and hang it before the spirit tablet, which is also a fitting gesture.

(4) Celebrating birthdays is not necessary. However, to commemorate a milestone in life, one can have a celebration every ten or twenty years, gathering relatives and friends for a joyous occasion. But it is inappropriate to use this as an opportunity to receive gifts from others. If one has close relationships and wants to keep some mementos, they should be things that are worthy of remembrance and not extravagant.

(5) Other activities like "yinshou" and performing good deeds are meaningless gestures that can be ignored.

These are the improvements I envision. However, the best fundamental solution is to eliminate the element of money from gift-giving. But due to deeply ingrained customs, a sudden change is impossible. Therefore, these are the transitional improvements. I welcome the wise to offer their corrections.

A Corner for the Society

A Stroll Down the Alley 187

— Zeng Geng

On summer nights, the cage-like houses are unbearably hot, and the pesky mosquitoes swarm around, buzzing and launching fierce attacks. So, one has no choice but to escape from the confines and head to the streets and alleys to enjoy a bit of the breeze and find relief from the sweltering heat.

This is a narrow alley, dimly lit by a few lifeless electric lights. Spiderwebs cover the lampshades, and the light bulbs have turned yellow. Patches of plaster have peeled off the walls, and green moss grows at the base. The foul-smelling gutters run the length of the alley. However, the stagnant wastewater is filled with tiny, wriggling mosquito larvae. All of this paints a vivid picture of this dim alley.

People are lying on the ground in clusters, some chatting, some gambling, and some already fast asleep. "A horse leaves the Western Liang border..." A friend, who is a laborer, lies on the ground, swinging his legs and singing. Across from him, a group of people crouch on a mat, gambling with dominoes.

"Xi Li Hua La!" With a shuffle of the tiles, the dealer throws back his neck and sings, "Seven pairs, Heaven's Gate first touch, Dealer's third touch."

After shouting this, four or five people reach out with their rough hands to grab their hands.

"Oh, broken! Broken!... Alas, damn it, no luck!" The man at Heaven's Gate stacks his two dominoes together, slowly opens them, and sighs.

"Hey, Ah Wu, what's up?" asks the person on the left.

"Damn it, Bie Shi!" says the Heaven's Gate player. One hand ends, and the dealer wins from two players and pays out to one. After a moment, the gambling continues. "Hey, Monk, what's up?" Ah Wu asks the person on the right.

"Not good, three-way Monk knocking on a wooden fish," the Monk replies.

"Haha, Monk meets Monk, what a coincidence," the dealer says, laughing.

"Hey, Hey, Three-Head and Ah San are coming!" A child runs in from the alley entrance, saying urgently. Immediately, the gambling group descends into chaos, hurriedly putting their money in their pockets and hiding their dominoes under the mat. One by one, they pretend to be calmly chatting. A foreign patrolman and an Indian policeman walk into the alley, slowly strolling and looking at the people on both sides.

"Jia deli ma deli gambling copper money, go inside!" the Indian policeman says to the group with a smile.

"Ah San, we aren't gambling copper money," the Monk says to him with a cheeky grin.

After the patrolman leaves, they take out their gambling tools again and huddle together to gamble. The sounds of Bie Shi, Zhi Zun, Tian Gang, and Di Gang fill the corner of the alley in a cacophony. At the end of the alley, two old women are talking.

"Granny San, the weather is very hot today!" one old woman says with a Ningbo accent.

"Not wrong, Zhang Old Lady, the weather is terribly hot," another says with a Suzhou dialect.

"Granny San, you are very lucky. You have three sons, all of whom can earn money. Your eldest daughter-in-law is capable, your second daughter-in-law is filial, and your third daughter-in-law is beautiful. You truly have it good, you've earned it in your past life," Zhang Old Lady says with envy.

"Oh my, you say that, but there are always troubles to be found."

"Smack!" Zhang Old Lady slaps her arm and curses, "Damn it, unlucky mosquitoes, so annoying!" After cursing, she continues chatting with Granny San. In the quiet air, I can only hear their soft conversations, common phrases like "True Emperor," "Jade Emperor," and "Early grandchild," piercing my eardrums. Occasionally, I also hear Zhang Old Lady's mosquito slapping sounds and her cursing, "Damn it!"

Peering through the Western Mirror

Lovable Shanghai? 188

— Yi Ping

"Ah! Shanghai, lovable Shanghai!"

A motorboat flies across the water like an arrow. Vaguely, a group of urban men and women sing this melodious song like a nightingale flying into my ears.

Standing beneath a tall building, I am deeply moved. Whether Shanghai is lovable can only be determined by those who have lived in Shanghai for at least three months. They will know that it is a prostitute suffering from a virulent sexually transmitted disease. Although it is alluring on the surface.

According to the Water Patrol Police Department, more than ten floating corpses were recovered from the Huangpu River last week. Upon closer examination, the reasons for these suicides were primarily

(1) Economic oppression

(2) Rejection in love

Other reasons were rare.

Shanghai has tall buildings, night gardens, dance halls... For those who indulge in pleasure and live in a drunken dream, it is, of course, a lovable place. However, in our large nation with its underdeveloped production and lack of widespread education, it is already a great fortune for people to be able to work from morning till night and still have enough to eat. Since the Shanghai Battle, many more friends have been unemployed. Economic oppression completes their suicide attempts in the Huangpu River. This is only a passive type of person. The more active initially try their luck through gambling; then they fall to become thugs. Thus, Shanghai has become a den of bandits where one's life is in danger when going out.

A bad environment can change people's personalities. Women are inherently prone to vanity (according to physiologists). Thus, love problems in Shanghai have become transactions of sex, and the parties involved are wearing tinted glasses, unaware of how to extricate themselves. Because the Shanghai they see is this kind of Shanghai. Furthermore, many frivolous films and novels clearly show that love is merely a check,

"A dull life!" Generally, young people shout loudly, finally they write a few sensual poems then go to the Huangpu River. Today, the newspapers reported a news item about bestiality in this city. It involved an oppressed eleven-year-old girl. This inhuman behavior was discovered in broad daylight, showing that Shanghai has no land(?), or national and personal standards.

Wealthy patrons who have enjoyed everything Shanghai has to offer have not seen this novel performance. Spending six yuan doesn't bother them. Harming the life of a young girl is even less of a concern to them. Chen Xinzhai spent money to buy a girl, of course, to sell her at a high price in the curious and corrupt minds of Shanghainese. How does the miss who sings "Ah! Shanghai, lovable Shanghai!" feel about this bizarre drama of bestiality?

Ah! Shanghai, lovable Shanghai?

Worldly Discussions

Women "Out" and Men "In" 189

— Hong Shou

The times are changing like an illusion, and everything is relentlessly passing. Ancient maxims once considered the gold standard are being overturned one by one. People are also being anesthetized and immersed by the times, forgetting the reasons why. As time passes, they feel that the present is right and the past is wrong. It's no wonder several senior gentlemen sigh deeply.

Opening the "Instructions for the Women's Quarters," one can't help but laugh. Why? It's the times. But what exactly is civilization? No one can say. Civilization is a vague thing? Perhaps what is considered a tremendous act of civilization now will be laughed at by more civilized people thousands of years from now.

In the past, there was an old saying, "Men should be out and women should be in." What does this mean? It means that men should be outward-looking, and women should stay at home, secluded and rarely venturing out. Just taking clothes as an example, women used to wear skirts that covered their toes when going out, and they didn't easily show their delicate hands to others. If a woman ran around in the streets, it was simply ridiculous. The times are different! Women bare their arms, legs, and chests, liberating themselves to the extreme. A portion of the women run around outside all day, calling it socializing, but men still wear long robes and pants. Except for the head that must breathe and the two hands that must work, the rest is completely wrapped in clothing. This phenomenon is now uniform both domestically and abroad. You see, foreigners always dress stiffly for ordinary days or banquets, while women show more and more skin. This is the reality.

I really don't understand why men are so stupid and don't know how to liberate themselves. I strongly agree with Mr. Zhang Cangsu's suggestion for improving men's clothing published in this newspaper. I hope it will be even more liberated, so that we men can also be "out."

Announcement Mr. Chen Jiaqing Xiuyuan of Ningxiang requested publication of his correspondence address for contact purposes. - Editorial Department

This ruling. ▲One case: Wang Xiaoshi's petition for release: The petition is acknowledged. Order the reliable shop guarantor to come to the court for further verification. This ruling. ▲One case: Cao Zhencheng's petition for amnesty: According to Article 1 of the Amnesty Ordinance, "All crimes committed before March 5, 1932, in which the most severe principal punishment is imprisonment of three years or less, detention, or a special fine, shall be pardoned." The petitioner committed the crime on March 6th of this year, which does not comply with the aforementioned ordinance. The petition for amnesty should be denied. This ruling. The plaintiff's other claims are rejected, and the litigation costs shall be borne by the defendants in proportion. ▲ The case of Xu Fuquan and Huang Zhanggui's payment for goods, the defendant shall pay the plaintiff $131, and the litigation costs shall be borne by the defendant. ▲ The case of Huang Xingbei and Zhang Quicheng et al.'s land and compensation, the disputed land of 1.1 hao is registered, and the defendant Zhang Quicheng shall return it to the plaintiff for management. The plaintiff's other claims are rejected, one-third of the litigation costs shall be borne by the plaintiff, and two-thirds shall be borne by the defendant Zhang Quicheng. ▲ The case of Yang Maomao and Zhang Xuefu's loan, the defendant shall repay the plaintiff's loan of $40, and the litigation costs shall be borne by the defendant. ▲ The case of Gu Jingqing and Bao Wenli et al.'s rent, the defendant Bao Wenli shall pay the plaintiff's rent of $28.80, excluding the one-fifth of the litigation costs for the withdrawn part to be borne by the plaintiff, the remainder shall be borne by the defendant Bao Wenli (one-fifth) and Feng Fujin (three-fifths). ▲ The case of Deng Jiechen and Wang Chengyin's annulment of marriage and handover of person, the marriage between Wang Chengyin and Deng Xiaobao shall be annulled, Wang Chengyin shall hand over Deng Shanbao to the plaintiff for retrieval, and the litigation costs shall be borne by the defendant.
